<P style="line-height:17pt; margin:0px" align=center><B>FOR THE PERIOD ENDED SEPTEMBER 30, 2008 </B></P>

<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:48px; padding-right:9.6px; text-indent:-24px"><B>1.</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px; padding-right:9.6px; text-indent:-12px"><B>NATURE OF OPERATIONS</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px" align=justify>ALDA Pharmaceuticals Corp. (the &#147;Company&#148;) was incorporated under the Company Act of British Columbia on May 30, 2000 and was classified as a Capital Pool Company as defined by the policies of the TSX Venture Exchange (the &#147;Exchange)&#148;. &nbsp;The Company completed its required Qualifying Transaction on November 13, 2003, at which point it ceased to be a Capital Pool Company, and its shares resumed trading on the Exchange effective November 19, 2003.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px" align=justify>The Company&#146;s main business activity is the development, production and marketing of infection control agent products, principally a product marketed as T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP> Disinfectant. &nbsp;Effective November 26, 2003, the name of the Company was changed from Duft Biotech Capital Ltd. to ALDA Pharmaceuticals Corp. </P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-right:9.6px"><B>2.</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-right:9.6px; text-indent:24px"><B>SIGNIFICANT ACCOUNTING POLICIES</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:52.8px; text-indent:-24px" align=justify>a)</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:52.8px; text-indent:-4.8px" align=justify>Basis of presentation</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px" align=justify>The Company prepares its financial statements in accordance with Canadian generally accepted accounting principles. &nbsp;These consolidated financial statements include the accounts of the Company and its wholly-owned subsidiary, Sirona Therapeutics Corp. (&#147;Sirona&#148;). &nbsp;The name of the subsidiary was changed on January 10, 2006 from ALDA Institute For Preventative Health Care Inc. &nbsp;Sirona is an inactive company, the shares of which were acquired pursuant to an asset purchase agreement. &nbsp;All significant inter-company balances and transactions have been eliminated on consolidation.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:24px" align=justify>b)</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:24px" align=justify>Cash and equivalents</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px" align=justify>Cash and equivalents include cash and highly liquid market instruments with original terms to maturity of less than ninety days at the time of acquisition.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:24px" align=justify>c)</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:24px" align=justify>Accounts receivable</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px" align=justify>Accounts receivable is presented net of allowance for doubtful accounts. &nbsp;The allowance for doubtful accounts reflects estimates of probable losses in accounts receivable. &nbsp;The allowance is determined based on balances outstanding for over 90 days from the invoice date, historical experience and other current information. &nbsp;The Company extends credit to customers and distributors; credit checks are required for all new distributors.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:24px" align=justify>d)</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:24px" align=justify>Inventory</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px" align=justify>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px" align=justify>Inventory is comprised of finished goods and related raw materials. &nbsp;Finished goods are reported at the lesser of cost and estimated net realizable value. &nbsp;Raw materials are reported at the lesser of cost and replacement cost. &nbsp;Inventory is determined using the first in, first out cost flow assumption.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><BR>
<BR></P>
<P style="line-height:10pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-13.333px; font-size:8pt">ALDA 2008-09-30 Interim Financials Q1</P>
<P style="line-height:10pt; margin:0px; text-indent:549.933px; font-size:8pt">Page 4<BR>
- ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------</P>

<P style="margin:0px" align=center><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px"><B>2.</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; text-indent:24px"><B>SIGNIFICANT ACCOUNTING POLICIES (CONTINUED)</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:24px" align=justify>e) </P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:24px" align=justify>Furniture and equipment</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px; text-indent:48px" align=justify>Furniture and equipment is recorded at cost and is amortized using the following annual rates:</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:72px" align=justify>Furniture and fixtures</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:360px" align=justify>20% Straight line</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:72px" align=justify>Computer equipment</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:360px" align=justify>30% Straight line</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:72px" align=justify>Computer software</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:360px" align=justify>30% Straight line</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px" align=justify>For the year of acquisition, the rate is one-half of the above.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:24px" align=justify>f)</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:24px" align=justify>Impairment of long-lived assets</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px" align=justify>The Company reviews for impairment of long-lived assets, including patent application and development costs, intangible assets, and furniture and equipment, on an annual basis or whenever circumstances indicate that the carrying amount of an asset may not be recoverable from expected future cash flows. &nbsp;The assessment of recoverability is made based on projected undiscounted future net cash flows that are directly associated with the asset&#146;s use and eventual disposition. &nbsp;The amount of the impairment loss, if any, is measured as the amount by which the carrying amount of the asset exceeds its fair value, which is measured by discounted cash flows when quoted market prices are not available. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:24px" align=justify>g)</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:24px" align=justify>Patent application and development costs</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px" align=justify>Patent application and development costs include expenditures attributable to efforts by the Company to research and develop and bring to commercial production a new product, as well as to acquire legal protections for its proprietary products, such as trademarks and patents. &nbsp;Research costs are expensed in the period in which they are incurred. &nbsp;Development costs are charged as an expense in the period incurred except in circumstances where the market and technical feasibility of the product have been established, recovery of these costs can reasonably be regarded as assured, and future values can be realized, in which case such costs are capitalized. &nbsp;In the latter case, patent application and development costs are amortized on a systematic basis over the patent life of 20 years. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:24px" align=justify>h)</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:24px" align=justify>Intangible assets</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:43px" align=justify>The carrying values of intangible assets which are determined to have a finite useful life are amortized on a systematic basis over the useful life of 20 years. Intangible assets are subject to an impairment test on an annual basis, based on a comparison of the fair value of the intangible asset to its carrying value. &nbsp;The carrying value is adjusted for impairment as necessary and any excess of the carrying amount over the fair value of the intangible asset is charged to earnings in the period occurred.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:10pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-13.333px; font-size:8pt">ALDA 2008-09-30 Interim Financials Q1</P>
<P style="line-height:10pt; margin:0px; text-indent:549.933px; font-size:8pt">Page 5<BR>

<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px"><B>2.</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; text-indent:24px"><B>SIGNIFICANT ACCOUNTING POLICIES (CONTINUED)</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:24px" align=justify>i)</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:24px" align=justify>Revenue recognition</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px" align=justify>The revenue of the Company is primarily derived from the sale of the Company&#146;s T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP> product. &nbsp;Revenue is recognized at the time of shipment, at which point risks and rewards over ownership and title of transfer have passed to the customer. &nbsp;At the point of sale, the Company assesses whether collection of the amount billed to the customer is reasonably assured. &nbsp;If collection of the amount is not reasonably assured, the Company defers recognizing revenue until such point as collection is reasonably assured, usually upon receipt of payment. &nbsp;If the customer is not known to the Company, payment in advance is required and the revenue is recognized when the products are shipped.&nbsp; Revenue is recognized net of any expected sales return. &nbsp;Under the Company&#146;s current policy, return of products is not allowed unless inspection of a sample of the damaged products is required by the Company or the wr
ong products have been shipped by the Company.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:24px" align=justify>j)</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:24px" align=justify>Income taxes</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px" align=justify>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px" align=justify>Income taxes are recorded using the asset and liability method whereby future tax assets and liabilities are recognized for the future tax consequences attributable to differences between the financial statement carrying amounts of existing assets and liabilities and their respective tax bases and operating loss carry forwards. &nbsp;Future tax assets and liabilities are measured using enacted or substantively enacted tax rates expected to apply when the asset is realized or the liability settled. &nbsp;The effect on future tax assets and liabilities of a change in tax rates is recognized in income in the year that substantive enactment or enactment occurs. &nbsp;To the extent that the Company does not consider it more likely than not that a future tax asset or portion thereof will be recovered, a valuation allowance is recorded.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:24px" align=justify>k)</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:24px" align=justify>Stock-based compensation </P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px" align=justify>The Company applies the fair value method of accounting for stock options. &nbsp;Under this method, fair value of options granted is determined using the Black-Scholes option pricing model and is recorded as stock-based compensation expense over the award&#146;s vesting period, with an offsetting amount recorded to contributed surplus. &nbsp;The amount is transferred from contributed surplus to share capital upon exercise of the option.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:24px" align=justify>l)</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:24px" align=justify>Share purchase warrants</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px" align=justify>The Company applies the fair value method of accounting for share purchase warrants. &nbsp;Under this method, proceeds received on issuance of units consisting of shares and warrants are allocated between contributed surplus and share capital based on their relative fair values, whereby the fair value of warrants is determined using the Black-Scholes option pricing model. &nbsp;The value of the warrants is transferred from contributed surplus to share capital upon exercise of the warrant.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:10pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-13.333px; font-size:8pt">ALDA 2008-09-30 Interim Financials Q1</P>

<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px"><B>2.</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; text-indent:24px"><B>SIGNIFICANT ACCOUNTING POLICIES (CONTINUED)</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:24px" align=justify>m)</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:24px" align=justify>Basis and diluted loss per share</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px" align=justify>Loss per share is calculated based on the weighted average number of common shares outstanding during the reported period. &nbsp;Basic loss per share is computed by dividing income available to common shareholders by the weighted average number of common shares outstanding in the year. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px" align=justify>The Company uses the treasury stock method to compute the dilutive effect of options, warrants and similar instruments. &nbsp;Under this method, the dilutive effect on loss per share is recognized on the use of the proceeds that could be obtained upon exercise of options, warrants and similar instruments. &nbsp;It assumes that the proceeds would be used to purchase common shares at the average market price during the year. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:24px" align=justify>n)</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:24px" align=justify>Measurement uncertainty</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px" align=justify>The preparation of these consolidated financial statements in accordance with Canadian generally accepted accounting principles requires management to make estimates and assumptions that affect the reported amount of assets and liabilities and the reported amount of revenues and expenses during the period. &nbsp;Areas requiring significant management estimates include valuation of intangible assets, estimated useful life of intangible assets, estimate useful life of patent application and development costs, stock based compensation expense, and valuation of share purchase warrants. &nbsp;Actual results could differ from these estimates.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:24px" align=justify>o)</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:24px" align=justify>Foreign Exchange</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px" align=justify>Assets and liabilities in U.S. dollars have been converted into Canadian dollars using the rate of exchange prevailing at September 30, 2008<I>. </I>&nbsp;Revenue and expenses were translated at the rate of exchange prevailing when the transactions were settled.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px"><B>3.</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; text-indent:24px"><B>ADOPTION OF NEW ACCOUNTING PRINCIPLES</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px" align=justify>The Company adopted the following new accounting standards issued by the Canadian Institute of Chartered Accountants (&#147;CICA&#148;) relating to comprehensive income, recognition, measurement, disclosure and presentation of financial instruments and hedges. &nbsp;These new accounting standards are applied prospectively beginning July 1, 2007. &nbsp;Adoption of these standards had no impact on the consolidated financial statements for the period ended September 30, 2008.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px" align=justify>Section 1530 &#150; Comprehensive Income &#150; This section established standards for reporting and presentation of a statement of comprehensive income. &nbsp;Comprehensive income includes net earnings and other comprehensive income. &nbsp;Other comprehensive income is defined as the change in equity from transactions and other events from non owner sources. &nbsp;Other comprehensive income includes holding gains and losses on certain derivative instruments that are classified as available-for-sale, and gains or losses due to the change in foreign currency relating to self-sustaining foreign operations, all of which are not recognized in net earnings until realized. &nbsp;&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><BR>
<BR></P>
<P style="line-height:10pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-13.333px; font-size:8pt">ALDA 2008-09-30 Interim Financials Q1</P>

<P style="line-height:17pt; margin:0px" align=center><B>NOTES TO THE CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS</B></P>
<P style="line-height:17pt; margin:0px" align=center><B>FOR THE PERIOD ENDED SEPTEMBER 30, 2008</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px"><B>3. </B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; text-indent:24px"><B>ADOPTION OF NEW ACCOUNTING PRINCIPLES (CONTINUED)</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px" align=justify>Section 3251 &#150; Equity &#150; In addition to Section 1530 (Comprehensive Income), this section establishes standards for the presentation of equity and changes in equity during the reporting period. </P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px" align=justify>Section 3855 &#150; Financial Instruments &#150; Recognition and Measurement &#150; This section established standards for recognizing and measuring financial instruments in the balance sheets and specifying how unrealized or realized gains and losses are to be presented during the reporting period. &nbsp;In accordance with the new accounting standard, all financial assets and financial liabilities are measured at fair value on initial recognition except for certain related party transaction.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px" align=justify>Financial instruments have been classified as held-to-maturity, available-for-sale, held for trading, loans and receivables, or other financial liabilities. &nbsp;Financial assets that are held to maturity, other than those held for trading, are measured at amortized cost. &nbsp;Available-for-sale instruments are measured at fair value with unrealized gains and losses recognized in other comprehensive income until realized, at which time realized gains and losses will be recognized in net income. &nbsp;Held for trading instruments are measured at fair value with unrealized gains and losses recognized in the results of operations in the period in which they arise. &nbsp;Loans and receivables are measured at amortized cost using the effective interest method. &nbsp;Any gains or losses on the realization of loans and receivables are included in earnings. &nbsp;Financial liabilities that are not classified as held to maturity are classified as other financia
l liabilities, and are carried at amortized costs using the effective interest method. &nbsp;Any gains and losses on realization of other financial liabilities are included in earnings. &nbsp;Any transaction costs incurred to acquire financial instruments will be included in earnings.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px" align=justify>The Company&#146;s financial instruments consist of cash and equivalents, accounts receivable, prepaid expenses and others, subscriptions receivable, and accounts payable and accrued liabilities. &nbsp;The fair value of these instruments approximates the carrying amounts due to the immediate or short-term maturity of these financial instruments. The Company has made the following classifications:</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:72px" align=justify>Cash and equivalents</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:405.933px" align=justify>Held for trading</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:72px" align=justify>Accounts receivable</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:378.533px" align=justify>Loans and receivable</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:72px" align=justify>Prepaids expenses and others</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:378.533px" align=justify>Loans and receivable</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:72px" align=justify>Subscriptions receivable</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:378.533px" align=justify>Loans and receivable</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:72px" align=justify>Accounts payable and accrued liabilities</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:358.267px" align=justify>Other financial liabilities</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px" align=justify>Section 3861 &#150; Financial Instruments &#150; Disclosure and Presentation &#150; This section establishes standards for presentation of financial instruments and non-financial derivates and identifies the information that should be disclosed about them. &nbsp;This section establishes standards for presentation of financial instruments and identifies the information which should be disclosed about them. &nbsp;Under the new standards, policies followed for years prior to the effective date are generally not reversed, and therefore the comparative figures have not been restated.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px" align=justify>Section 3862 &#150; Financial Instruments &#150; Disclosures and Section 3863 &#150; Financial Instruments &#150; Presentation - These sections revised and enhance the disclosure requirements while carrying forward its presentation requirements. &nbsp;These new sections will place increased emphasis on disclosures about the nature and extent of risks associated with both recognized and unrecognized financial instruments, how the entity manages the risks, and the exposure to liquidity, currency and other price risks.</P>

<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px"><B>3. </B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; text-indent:24px"><B>ADOPTION OF NEW ACCOUNTING PRINCIPLES (CONTINUED)</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px" align=justify>It is management&#146;s opinion that the Company is not exposed to significant interest, currency, credit, and liquidity risk arising from these financial instruments. &nbsp;The Company has transactions dominated in US dollars but exposure to currency risk is immaterial. &nbsp;The Company mitigates its exposure to credit risk by maintaining its primary operating accounts with chartered bank in Canada and constantly monitoring credit standing of counterparties. &nbsp;The Company manages its liquidity risk through the management of its capital as described in note 14. &nbsp;The Company does not use financial derivatives.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px" align=justify>Section 3865 &#150; Hedges &#150; This section establishes standards for the Company that chooses to designate qualifying transactions as hedges for accounting purposes. &nbsp;This section builds on Accounting Guideline AcG-13, &#147;Hedging Relationships,&#148; and Section 1650, &#147;Foreign Currency Translation&#148;. &nbsp;The Company does not use hedge accounting and has no hedging relationships.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px" align=justify>Section 1535, &#147;Capital Disclosures&#148; &#150; This section establishes standards for disclosing information about an entity&#146;s capital and how it is managed. &nbsp;It requires the disclosure of the entity&#146;s objectives, policies and processes for managing capital as well as summary quantitative data on the elements included in the management of capital. </P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px" align=justify>Section 3031 &#150; &#147;Inventories&#148; &#150; This section establishes standards for measuring the inventories. &nbsp;The new standards require that the inventories shall be measured at the lower of cost and the net realizable value. &nbsp;This section provides guidelines on the determination of cost and its subsequent recognition as an expense, including any write-down to net realizable value and reversal of a previous write-down when the value of inventories is evidently increased due to the change in economic circumstances. &nbsp;The use of last-in, first-out method (LIFO) in measuring inventories is not recommended. This section applies to interim and annual financial statements for fiscal years beginning on or after January 1, 2008. &nbsp;The Company is evaluating the effect of adopting this new standard.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px" align=justify>Section 3064 &#150; &#147;Goodwill and Intangible Assets&#148; &#150; The replacement of Section 3062 establishes standards for the recognition, measurement, presentation and disclosure of goodwill and intangible assets. &nbsp;The Company is evaluating the impact of this new standard.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px" align=justify>As announced by the Canadian Accounting Standards Board (&#147;AcSB&#148;), the financial reporting requirements for Canadian companies will be changed to the use of International Financial Reporting Standards (&#147;IFRS&#148;), replacing Canada&#146;s own GAAP. &nbsp;The changeover date for publicly-listed companies is 2011. &nbsp;The Company has begun reviewing its plan for adopting IFRS for 2011. &nbsp;At this time, the Company has not yet determined the financial reporting impact due to the change of new reporting standards.</P>

<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:24px" align=justify>a)</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:24px" align=justify>Share Capital (continued)</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:72px; text-indent:-24px" align=justify>i)</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:72px" align=justify>On August 14, 2007, the Company completed a private placement of 2,000,000 units of the Company at a price of $0.12 per unit for gross proceeds of $240,000. &nbsp;Each unit consists of one common share of the Company and one share purchase warrant. &nbsp;Each warrant entitles the holder to acquire one additional common share at a price of $0.24 per share until August 13, 2008 and, thereafter at a price of $0.36 per share until August 13, 2009. &nbsp;Finders&#146; fees and legal fees in the amount of $13,920 were charged against shares capital in connection with the private placement. &nbsp;Warrants were valued at 90,108.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:72px; text-indent:-24px" align=justify>ii)</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:72px" align=justify>On November 22, 2007, the Company completed a private placement of 3,500,000 units of the Company at a price of $0.15 per unit for gross proceeds of $525,000. &nbsp;Each unit consists of one common share of the Company and one share purchase warrant. &nbsp;Each warrant entitles the holder to acquire one additional common share at a price of $0.30 per share until November 22, 2008 and, thereafter at a price of $0.45 per share until November 22, 2009. &nbsp;5% finder&#146;s fee in the amount of $15,750 was to satisfied by the delivery of 82,895 common shares of the Company at a &nbsp;deemed price per share of $0.19. &nbsp;&nbsp;Legal fees in the amount of $5,953 were charged against shares capital in connection with the private placement. Warrants were valued at $188,943.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:72px; text-indent:-24px" align=justify>iii) </P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:72px" align=justify>During the year ended June 30, 2008, 650,000 options and 11,086,500 warrants were exercised by the holders at an exercise price range of $0.10 to $0.11 per option for total gross proceeds of $67,000 and at an exercise price range of $0.10 to $0.30 per warrant for total gross proceeds of 1,918,200. &nbsp;Options value of $29,000 and warrants value of $385,147 previously recorded in contributed surplus for options and warrants were credited to share capital, respectively.</P>

<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px"><B>7.</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; text-indent:24px"><B>SHAREHOLDERS&#146; EQUITY (CONTINUED)</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:24px">b)</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:24px">Stock options (Continued)</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:72px; text-indent:-24px" align=justify>(i)</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:72px" align=justify>On December 12, 2007, the Company granted options to acquire 1,820,000 common shares of the Company to directors, consultants, officers, employees and investor relations. &nbsp;The options have an exercise price of $0.50 with an exercisable term of three years expiring December 7, 2010. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:72px; text-indent:-24px" align=justify>(ii)</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:72px" align=justify>1,270,000 options vested immediately with an estimated fair value of $0.26 per share resulting $333,404 in stock based compensation expense being recognized. &nbsp;550,000 options shall be vested in equal quarterly installment over a period of 12 to 24 months from the date of grant.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:72px; text-indent:-24px" align=justify>(iii)</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:72px" align=justify>On May 2, 2008, the Company granted options to acquire 1,150,000 common shares of the Company to directors, consultants, officers, employees and investor relations. &nbsp;The options have an exercise price of $0.80 with an exercisable term of three years expiring May 2, 2011. &nbsp;1,050,000 options vested immediately with an estimated fair value of $0.47 per share resulting $489,234 in stock based compensation expense being recognized. &nbsp;100,000 options shall be vested in equally quarterly installment over a period of 12 months from the date of grant.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:72px; text-indent:-24px" align=justify>(iv)</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:72px" align=justify>During the three month period ended September 30, 2008, 380,000 options were exercised at an exercise price of $0.10 for total gross proceeds of $38,000</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>

<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:28.8px; text-indent:-28.8px" align=justify><B>9.</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:28.8px; text-indent:-4.8px" align=justify><B>RELATED PARTY TRANSACTIONS</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:48px; text-indent:-24px" align=justify>a)</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px" align=justify>During the three month period ended September 30, 2008, the Company paid consulting fees of $81,000 (September 30, 2007: $54,000) to companies controlled by directors of the Company.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:48px; text-indent:-24px" align=justify>b)</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px" align=justify>During the three month period ended September 30, 2008, the Company paid rent of $6,580 (September 30, 2007: $6,493) to a company controlled by a director of the Company.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:30.267px" align=justify>These transactions were measured at the exchange amount, which is the amount of consideration established and agreed to by the related parties.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px"><B>10.</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; text-indent:24px"><B>CAPITAL DISCLOSURES</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px" align=justify>The Company&#146;s objectives when managing capital is to maintain sufficient cash resources to support its research and development activities, pre-clinical trial program, intellectual property protection and expansion on its T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP> technology. &nbsp;The Company includes shareholders&#146; equity and cash and its equivalent in the definition of capital. &nbsp;The Company does not have any debt obligation other than trade accounts payable. &nbsp;&nbsp;The availability of capital is solely through the issuance of the Company&#146;s common shares. &nbsp;The Company will not issue additional equity until such time when the fund is needed and the market condition becomes favorable to the Company. There are no assurances that the fund will be made available to the Company when required. The Company makes every effort to safeguard its capital and minimize the dilution to its shareholders. </P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px" align=justify>The Company is not subject to any externally imposed capital requirements. </P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px"><B>11.</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; text-indent:24px"><B>SUBSEQUENT EVENTS</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px" align=justify>Subsequent to the three month period ended September 30, 2008, the Company granted incentive stock options to certain directors, senior officers, employees and consultants to purchase an aggregate of 550,000 common shares at an exercise price of $0.20 and a term of five years, expiring on October 31, 2008. </P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px"><B>12.</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; text-indent:24px"><B>COMPARATIVE FIGURES</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px" align=justify>Certain comparative figures have been reclassified to conform to the presentation adopted in the current period.<B> </B></P>

<P style="line-height:27.6pt; margin-top:9.6px; margin-bottom:0px; font-size:12pt" align=center>December 1, 2008</P>
<P style="line-height:27.6pt; margin-top:12.8px; margin-bottom:0px"><BR></P>
</DIV><DIV style="width:624px"><P style="margin-top:126.667px; margin-bottom:0px" align=justify><I>The statements contained in this report that are not purely historical are forward-looking statements. &#147;Forward looking statements &#148; include statements regarding our expectations, hopes, intentions or strategies regarding the future. <BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; page-break-before:always" align=center><B>ALDA PHARMACEUTICALS CORP</B>.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center>MANAGEMENT DISCUSSION AND ANALYSIS (&#147;MD&amp;A&#148;)</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center>FOR THE THREE MONTH PERIOD ENDED SEPTEMBER 30, 2008</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-bottom:4px; border-bottom:1px solid #000000" align=center><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:110.4px"><B>1.1</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:110.4px; text-indent:32.867px"><B>DATE</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>This Management Discussion and Analysis (&#147;MD&amp;A&#148;) is dated December 1, 2008 and should be read in conjunction with the consolidated financial statements of ALDA Pharmaceuticals Corp. (&#147;ALDA&#148; or the &#147;Company&#148;) for the financial year ended June 30, 2008. All financial information is expressed in Canadian dollars and is prepared in accordance with Canadian generally accepted accounting principles (&#147;GAAP&#148;). </P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>The financial statements have been prepared on a going concern basis, according to Section 1400 of the Canadian Institute of Chartered Accountants (&#147;CICA&#148;), which assumes the realization of assets and settlement of liabilities in the normal course of the business. The Company has yet to achieve a level of revenues adequate to achieve profitability. The application of the going concern assumption is dependent on management&#146;s ability to successfully execute its business plan, to secure sufficient financing, and to develop profitable operations. &nbsp;Management of the Company believes that it will succeed in meeting those objectives, allowing the continued operation of the company. &nbsp;Additional equity or debt-based financing is required to continue the Company&#146;s operations and pursue therapeutic developments.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:37.933px; text-indent:-33px" align=justify><B>1.2</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:37.933px" align=justify><B>OVERALL PERFORMANCE </B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>On November 13, 2003, ALDA Pharmaceuticals Corp., formerly Duft Biotech Capital Ltd., completed the acquisition of the assets of 513947 BC Ltd., formerly ALDA Pharmaceuticals Inc., (&#147;the Qualifying Transaction&#148;) and a $1.2 Million financing arranged by Canaccord Capital Corporation (&#147;the Financing&#148;). ALDA trades on the TSX Venture Exchange in Vancouver, Canada under the symbol &#147;APH&#148;.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>ALDA has developed a patent-pending infection control formulation, referred to as T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP>, a mixture of ethanol, o-phenylphenol, benzalkonium chloride and other ingredients (including lemon fragrance and water). &nbsp;All of these component chemicals are bio-degradable.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify><B><U>Manufacturing and sales agreements</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify><B>Canada</B></P>
<P style="line-height:normal; margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>On October 4, 2005 the Company signed a manufacturing agreement with Norwood Packaging Ltd. (&#147;Norwood&#148;) of Surrey British Columbia, Canada to manufacture its T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174; </SUP>Disinfectant antibacterial product.<FONT style="font-family:Times; font-size:12pt"> </FONT><FONT style="font-family:Times">On June 18</FONT>, 2008, both the Company and Norwood agreed to waive the 90 day notice period required in the agreement and to terminate the agreement. For future orders, ALDA will provide Norwood with purchase orders and pay Norwood according to the standard payment terms that Norwood provides to its other customers. The Company has also started to use other manufacturers.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>An agreement between Group 270 Sales and Marketing Inc. (&#147;Group 270&#148;) and ALDA was established on November 17, 2006 in which Group 270 will assist ALDA in selling ALDA&#146;s products in the retail market. To accomplish this, Group 270 will undertake market research and a competitive analysis to estimate total annual volume in the area of personal disinfectants, estimate annual sales volumes, establish the pricing structure for retail and establish a roll out strategy to national retail chains, such as Shoppers Drug Mart, Loblaws, Wal-Mart and Zellers, sourcing and engaging a third party logistics company for order fulfillment, establish EDI and order processing development.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>On August 22, 2008 Group 270 and the Company mutually agreed that Group 270 will be compensated at the rate of $100 per hour rather than receiving a monthly retainer. In the event that both ALDA and Group 270 mutually agree that there is sufficient reason to continue the payment, it will remain in effect on a month to month basis until the payment of a commission rate of 8% of net sales exceeds the $1,500 per month. At that time the monthly payment will cease and Group 270 will receive only the commission.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><BR>
<BR></P>
<P style="line-height:10pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-13.333px; font-size:8pt">ALDA 2008-03-30 Q1 MD&amp;A</P>
<P style="line-height:10pt; margin:0px; text-indent:549.933px; font-size:8pt">Page 1<BR>
- ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
</DIV><DIV style="width:600px"><P style="line-height:14pt; margin:0px; text-indent:568px; font-size:12pt; page-break-before:always">&nbsp;&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
</DIV><DIV style="width:624px"><P style="margin:0px" align=center><B>ALDA PHARMACEUTICALS CORP</B>.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center>MANAGEMENT DISCUSSION AND ANALYSIS (&#147;MD&amp;A&#148;)</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center>FOR THE THREE MONTH PERIOD ENDED SEPTEMBER 30, 2008</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-bottom:4px; border-bottom:1px solid #000000" align=center><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; text-indent:6.667px" align=justify><B><U>Manufacturing and sales agreements (continued)</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>The agreement may be terminated if either party provides the other party with 60 days written notice, by either party if there has been a breach of any provision of the agreement and thirty (30) days has elapsed from the date that written notice has been sent to the party in breach by the other party or at the option of either party, if the other party becomes insolvent; violates the laws, regulations, rules, or statutes of any government; ceases doing business; makes an assignment for the benefit of creditors; or commits an act of bankruptcy. A failure by either party to exercise any right hereunder shall not operate as a waiver of such right and all remedies contained within the agreement shall be cumulative. </P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify><B>China</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>On October 6, 2004, ALDA entered into an agreement with Fuzhou Xinmei Biotech Co. Ltd. (&#147;Fuzhou&#148;) to manufacture and distribute ALDA&#146;s products Fujian province in China. On August 31, 2006, an agent acting on behalf of Fuzhou (&#147;the Agent&#148;), received a Certificate of Approval from the Fujian Centre of Disease Control for T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174; </SUP>Disinfectant after passing all of the required tests. The registration of T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP> Disinfectant in China was expanded beyond disinfection of inanimate objects, such as hospital equipment and instruments, to also allow external use on humans, including use as a first-aid antiseptic and hand sanitizer. The Certificate of Approval allowed the Agent to apply to the Chinese National Centre for Health Inspection and Supervision for approval to manufacture T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174; </SUP>Disinfectant for sale in China and for export. On April 19, 2007, a manufactu
ring certificate (Certificate of Approval (Health ID. No. 0109) was granted to the Agent in China for a period of four years from April 19, 2007 to April 18, 2011 and is renewable by filing an application for renewal 6 months before the expiry date.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>In May 25, 2007, ALDA&#146;s agent in China established a new company, He-Yi She Ye Limited (&#147;He-Yi&#148;) and the agreement with Fuzhou was transferred to He-Yi and expanded to cover marketing in all of China. The agreement with He-Yi provides that ALDA will provide He-Yi with all information that ALDA has at its disposal to assist with the registration of ALDA&#146;s products in China. In the agreement, it is stated that He-Yi will be responsible for procuring all necessary government approvals for ALDA&#146;s products within 6 months from the time all technical data to support the application is provided by ALDA Pharmaceuticals Corp. Quarterly reports on the progress of the approvals will be provided to ALDA by He-Yi. Extensions may be requested by He-Yi to procure all necessary government approvals and may not be unreasonably refused by ALDA for recurring periods of 3 months if He-Yi is employing its best efforts in obtaining the registration
 of the ALDA products in China and is providing quarterly reports as required or more time is required by ALDA Pharmaceuticals Corp. to obtain information required by He-Yi. As noted above, He-Yi has now fulfilled its obligations to register T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP> Disinfectant for sale in China.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>Under the terms of the agreement, ALDA Pharmaceuticals Corp. will provide He-Yi with the specifications required for He-Yi to provide a manufacturing facility suitable for the manufacturing of ALDA&#146;s products. He-Yi will provide a fully equipped manufacturing facility according to the specifications provided by ALDA, to produce the ALDA products subject to He-Yi employing its best efforts to obtain the space, materials and equipment specified by ALDA and He-Yi will have the right to distribute ALDA&#146;s products in China subject to ALDA&#146;s approval of each distributorship. As announced in a news release distributed by the Company on May 29, 2008, He-Yi has fulfilled it&#146;s obligation to establish a manufacturing facility.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><BR>
<BR></P>
</DIV><DIV style="width:600px"><P style="line-height:10pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-13.333px; font-size:8pt">ALDA 2008-03-30 Q1 MD&amp;A</P>
<P style="line-height:10pt; margin:0px; text-indent:549.933px; font-size:8pt">Page 2<BR>

<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin:0px; text-indent:568px; font-size:12pt; page-break-before:always">&nbsp;&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
</DIV><DIV style="width:624px"><P style="margin:0px" align=center><B>ALDA PHARMACEUTICALS CORP</B>.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center>MANAGEMENT DISCUSSION AND ANALYSIS (&#147;MD&amp;A&#148;)</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center>FOR THE THREE MONTH PERIOD ENDED SEPTEMBER 30, 2008</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-bottom:4px; border-bottom:1px solid #000000" align=center><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify><B><U>Manufacturing and sales agreements (continued)</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>The Agreement is effective until April 18, 2011 (&#147;the Initial Term&#148;). &nbsp;Upon expiration of the Initial Term, the Agreement may be renewed for additional periods, (&#147;the Renewals&#148;) provided that ALDA and He-Yi have each met all of their obligations under the Agreement and provided that He-Yi is able to obtain renewals of the Certificate of Approval (Health ID. No. 0109) that has been granted by the Ministry of Health of the People&#146;s Republic of China and expires on April 18, 2011. Any renewals will reflect current market conditions in the territory served by He-Yi at the time the Renewals are granted and the time periods of any Renewals will be the same as the corresponding time periods of the renewals of the Certificate</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>For the first 3 years after production is started by He-Yi and within 6 months after production is started by He-Yi, ALDA and He-Yi will establish minimum sales levels and, thereafter, after each new distributorship is established.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>He-Yi will pay ALDA a royalty, based on the gross revenues received by He-Yi for all of ALDA&#146;s products sold in China as follows:</P>
<P style="line-height:10pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-13.333px; padding-left:96px; text-indent:-24px; font-family:Symbol; font-size:8pt" align=justify>&#183;</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:96px" align=justify>5% during the first and second year after production is started by He-Yi, </P>
<P style="line-height:10pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-13.333px; padding-left:96px; text-indent:-24px; font-family:Symbol; font-size:8pt" align=justify>&#183;</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:96px" align=justify>8% during the third year,</P>
<P style="line-height:10pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-13.333px; padding-left:96px; text-indent:-24px; font-family:Symbol; font-size:8pt" align=justify>&#183;</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:96px" align=justify>6% after a doubling of sales over the sales achieved in the second year has occurred.</P>
<P style="line-height:10pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-13.333px; padding-left:96px; text-indent:-24px; font-family:Symbol; font-size:8pt" align=justify>&#183;</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:96px" align=justify>He-Yi will pay ALDA a 10% royalty based on the gross revenues received by He-Yi for all of ALDA&#146;s products sold by He-Yi outside of China.</P>
<P style="line-height:10pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-13.333px; padding-left:96px; text-indent:-24px; font-family:Symbol; font-size:8pt" align=justify>&#183;</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:96px" align=justify>All royalties will be paid monthly within 30 days after each month end.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>ALDA, at ALDA&#146;s discretion, will have the right to buy product from He-Yi. At the request of ALDA and with the authorization of ALDA, He-Yi agrees to direct ship ALDA&#146;s products for ALDA, at ALDA&#146;s expense, to anywhere in the world.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>As of the date of this report, the agreement is in good standing. On April 8, 2008, the Company announced that He-Yi had secured four contracts for the distribution of T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174; </SUP>Disinfectant in China. Evergreen Health Care committed to minimum sales of 1 million RMB in Hong Kong and Macau for a period of one year, Jin Wei Kai Medical Technology Limited and Jin Qin Scientific Development Ltd. to 4.8 Million RMB each over three years in northern China (Beijing) and central China (Wu Hang), respectively, and Wondfo Biotech Co. Ltd. to 3 million RMB in southern China (Guang Zhou) over three years. The total sales potential of all four contracts is 13.6 Million RMB or nearly CDN $2 million at the current exchange rate. The Company will realize a royalty as described above on any sales achieved by He-Yi. On May 29, 2008, the Company announced that the manufacturing facility set up in China by He-Yi was operational and that the first pr
oduction runs had started. In addition, a pilot batch of the T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174; </SUP>formulation that was manufactured by He-Yi passed the quality control and efficacy tests. At the time of this report, He-Yi was sourcing materials for the Company to use for the preparation of wipe canisters to contain T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174; </SUP>Disinfectant and T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP> &#147;Ready to Use&#148; Disinfectant Cleaner. He-Yi is also seeking registration of the T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174; </SUP>Disinfectant in gel form for use as a hand antiseptic. </P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify><B>United States</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>On December 13, 2007, the Company announced that the services of Brand Institute, Inc. had been engaged to assist with marketing efforts in the US and internationally, particularly with the development of the retail and therapeutic applications of the T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174; </SUP>technology. The Company saw a need to align its marketing efforts with its anticipated European and FDA product registrations and the proposed listing of its shares in the US. &nbsp;Due to its US and international presence, Brand Institute, Inc. was selected to work with the Company in its targeted markets. Brand Institute, Inc. offers pharmaceutical naming, packaging and labeling, trade marking and market research services, as well as global regulatory insight provided by former key officials from the FDA and Health Canada. With offices in the US, Europe and Asia, Brand Institute Inc. will provide strategic and regulatory assistance to the Company as it establishes its pr
esence in markets outside of Canada. Brand Institute is also assisting the Company with the re-design of its website and with other aspects of its retail marketing program such as label design and graphics. At the time of this report, only the website design is still outstanding. Due to the economic consitions prevailing at the time of this report, the Company is postponing this work in order to conserve cash.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>No other active sales or manufacturing agreements are in place. </P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>

<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
</DIV><DIV style="width:624px"><P style="margin:0px" align=center><B>ALDA PHARMACEUTICALS CORP</B>.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center>MANAGEMENT DISCUSSION AND ANALYSIS (&#147;MD&amp;A&#148;)</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center>FOR THE THREE MONTH PERIOD ENDED SEPTEMBER 30, 2008</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-bottom:4px; border-bottom:1px solid #000000" align=center><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; text-indent:6.667px" align=justify><B><U>Patents</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>The Company is attempting to patent or secure proprietary protection for the specific combination and manufacturing of the T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174; </SUP>formulation although the ingredients are all common chemical compounds. </P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>The Patent Cooperation Treaty (PCT) is an international patent law treaty established in 1970. It provides a unified procedure for filing patent applications to protect inventions in each of its Contracting States, which includes each jurisdiction specified below. A patent application filed under the PCT is called an &#147;international application&#148; or &#147;PCT application&#148;. A single filing of an international application is made with a Receiving Office (RO) in one language. It then results in a search being performed by an International Searching Authority (ISA), accompanied with a written opinion regarding the patentability of the invention which is the subject of the application. Optionally, this is followed by a preliminary examination, performed by an International Preliminary Examining Authority (IPEA). The PCT does not lead to the grant of an &quot;international patent&quot;, which does not exist, but rather, national patent examinat
ions that are handled by each relevant national or regional authority. For example, in Canada, the US, China, Australia and Singapore, there are national patent offices whereas, in Europe, the European Patent Office handles the national phase for its member states. </P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>API filed patent application #PCT/CA2002/001284, &#147;A wide spectrum disinfectant&#148;, on August 20, 2002. All rights to the patent application were transferred from API to the Company on completion of the Qualifying Transaction on November 13, 2003. A summary of subsequent events is presented below.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify><B>Canada</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>On February 18, 2005 the Canadian Intellectual Property Office (&#147;CIPO&#148;) received the PCT patent application and assigned it Patent Application Number 2,495,938. On August 17, 2007, the Company filed a Request for Examination with CIPO. On September 24, 2007 the Company filed a Voluntary Amendment to the patent application filed with CIPO. The proposed amendments expanded the claims to include a number of therapeutic applications of the T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP> formulation, including its use in cosmetics and in a microbicidal gel to prevent the transmission of sexually transmitted infections (&#147;STI&#146;s&#148;). On October 4, 2007, the Company was notified that CIPO had acknowledged a request by the Company to examine the patent application. Since the process of examination can take two years, for a fee of $500, the Company requested an Expedited Examination on November 7, 2007 to reduce the response time to approximately three mo
nths. On April 8, 2008, CIPO provided an Office Action in which a number of questions were posed to the Company. Many of the same questions had already been posed by the Examiner for the EPO. These will be addressed before the deadline of October 8, 2009. No further action was taken on the Canadian patent application as of the date of this report.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify><B>European Union</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>On March 30, 2005 the PCT application was accepted for national examination by the European Patent Office (&#147;EPO&#148;) which assigned it Patent Application Number 02754054.1-2113. The countries covered by the European patent application are Austria, Belgium, Bulgaria, Switzerland, Cyprus, the Czech Republic, Germany, Denmark, Estonia, Spain, Finland, France, Great Britain (the UK), Greece, Ireland, Italy, Liechtenstein, Luxembourg, Monaco, Netherlands, Portugal, Sweden, the Slovak Republic and Turkey. On May 18, 2005, the bibliographic data of the above-noted application was published in the European Patent Bulletin, under Publication No. 1530485. The resulting effect of such publication is that any possible infringer is deemed to have knowledge of the patent application without the Company having to formally inform them of this application&#146;s existence. On October 18, 2006 the EPO provided the Company with an Office Action requesting further
 information on the patent application. The Company responded to the questions and received a second Office Action, dated September 5, 2007 from the EPO. This second Office Action requested that the Company provide certain additional information and to conduct certain experiments to support the claims that were made in the application. As of the date of this report, the Company has completed the literature research required to provide the additional information required by the EPO. Certain laboratory studies have been conducted or are still in progress to fully address the questions raised by the EPO.</P>

<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify><B>China</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>On June 25, 2005 the Company was notified that the PCT application was accepted for national examination by the Patent Office of the People&#146;s Republic of China (&#147;Chinese Patent Office&#148;) and assigned Patent Application Number 02829642.7. On August 11, 2005, the Chinese Patent Office accepted a Request for Substantive Examination from the Company. The application was published in the Chinese Patent Gazette on October 19, 2005, under Publication No. CN1684711A and entered into Substantive Examination. On February 5, 2006, the Company filed a Voluntary Amendment to the original patent application to correct certain minor errors in the original application. On June 2, 2006, the Chinese Patent Office provided an Office Action which requested certain additional amendments to the patent application. On December 18, 2006, the Company filed its response to the Office Action. The Company was notified by the Chinese Patent Office that the Chinese p
atent had been allowed, effective June 8, 2007. During the quarter ended September 30, 2007, amendments to the original patent application were drafted. As in the case of the amendments prepared for CIPO, the proposed amendments to the Chinese patent expand the original claims to include a number of therapeutic applications of the T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP> formulation, including its use in cosmetics and in a microbicidal gel to prevent the transmission of sexually transmitted infections (&#147;STI&#146;s&#148;). &nbsp;On October 10, 2007, the Company was advised that the amended claims had been submitted to the Chinese Patent Office. On January 30, 2008 the Chinese Patent office assigned Chinese Divisional Patent Application No. 200710142798.3 to the new application which was published in the Chinese Patent Gazette, under Publication No. CN101112624A. At the time of this report, no further developments have occurred with this Chinese patent application. On February 6, 2008, the Company announced that C
ertificate of Invention Patent Number ZL02829642.7 had been issued by the State Intellectual Property Office of the People&#146;s Republic of China. The patent provides protection for the composition and production methods for ALDA&#146;s T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP> formulation until August 20, 2022. </P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify><B>United States</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>On February 18, 2005, the US Patent and Trademark Office (&#147;USPTO&#148;) received the PCT patent application and assigned it Patent Application Number 10/525,110. The patent application was published by the USPTO on December 22, 2005, under Publication Number US 2005/0282727. On July 27, 2006, the Company received that first Office Action from the USPTO which required clarification or modification of certain claims made in the patent application. The Company was required to respond to the Office Action by October 27, 2006 and did so on October 26, 2006 with amendments to the claims that required clarification or modification. On February 7, 2007 the USPTO provided the Company with a Notice of Allowance for the US patent with all claims made by the Company accepted by the USPTO. A Notice of Allowance is not a grant of a patent and is subject to withdrawal by the USPTO or on petition by the Company. The Company then filed certain minor, voluntary am
endments to the patent application and a second Notice of Allowance, dated June 8, 2007 was provided by the USPTO. During the quarter ended September 30, 2007, amendments to the original patent application were drafted. These amendments were submitted to the USPTO as a U.S. Continuation Patent Application in December, 2007. As in the case of the amendments prepared for the Chinese Patent Office and CIPO, the proposed amendments to the US patent expand the original claims to include a number of therapeutic applications of the T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP> formulation, including its use in cosmetics and in a microbicidal gel to prevent the transmission of sexually transmitted infections (&#147;STI&#146;s&#148;). On January 23, 2008 the USPTO issued a Filing Receipt for the U.S. Continuation Patent Application and assigned Serial No. 11/966,128 to the application. On February 15, 2008, the Company was advised that a Notice of Allowance had been received from the USPTO projecting that the US patent would be is
sued on March 4, 2008. As projected, U.S. Patent Number 7,338,927 was issued on that date and provides protection for the composition and production methods for ALDA's T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP> formulation until August 20, 2022. &nbsp;The patent can be viewed on the website of the USPTO. On May 2, 2008, the USPTO issued an Office action in response to U.S. Continuation Patent Application No. 11/966,128. A number of questions were posed to the Company and these were addressed by the company prior to the deadline of November 2, 2008.</P>

<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify><B>Australia</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>On March 15, 2005 the PCT application was accepted for national examination by the Australian patent office on March 15, 2005 and assigned with Patent Application Number 2002322916. On October 24, 2006, the Australian patent office provided the Company with a Direction to Request Examination. Under Australian Patent law, such examination must be requested within five years of the filing date or within six months of receiving a direction from the Australian Patent Office, whichever is sooner. On October 10, 2007 the Company announced that the Australian Patent Office had accepted the patent application with no objections. On December 4, 2007, a divisional application was filed at the Australian Patent Office. As in the case of the amendments prepared for the Chinese Patent Office, CIPO and the USPTO, the divisional application provides amendments to the Australian patent that expand the original claims to include a number of therapeutic applications of

On February 22, 2008, the Company announced that Australian Patent Number 2002322916 has been issued by the Australia Patent Office. The patent provides protection for the composition and production methods for ALDA&#146;s T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174; </SUP>formulation until August 20, 2022. On March 3, 2008, the Company was notified that the divisional application had been assigned Serial No. 2007237333 with an official filing date of August 20, 2002. Examination of the application was requested by the Company on June 3, 2008.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify><B><U>PCT application for anti-inflammatory, antiseptic therapeutic formulation</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>On March 20, 2008 the Company filed a comprehensive new patent application, International Application No. PCT/CA2008/000536, &#147;Antiseptic Compositions for the Treatment of Infections&#148;, with CIPO under the Patent Cooperation Treaty (PCT). The new PCT application seeks protection for the composition and preparation of T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174; </SUP>formulations that also contain steroids, anesthetics or analgesics for use on topical infections and, in particular, inflamed infections. Typically, infections with associated inflammation are treated with separate antiseptic and anti-inflammatory preparations. The new T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174; </SUP>formulations combine these properties into a single treatment, making the prescription process easier for the physician and the application easier for the patient.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>In preliminary studies, under the direction of a physician, T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174; </SUP>formulations containing anti-inflammatory steroids quickly resolved a number of skin infections, some of which had resisted all other treatments. Examples include chronic eczema with secondary Staphylococcus infections and fungal infections, such as athlete&#146;s foot, <I>Tinea versicolor</I>. As of the date of this report, there have been no developments with this PCT application</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>As the time of writing, the Company has no assurance that any patents that have not yet been granted will be granted at all and, if any patents are granted, the Company cannot estimate when the patents will be granted or what claims will be allowed and protected. </P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify><B><U>Trademarks</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>The Company successfully trademarked &#147;T36&#148; in Canada on April 22, 2004 and in the United States on November 2, 2004. &nbsp;The trademark in the United States is a Principal Register mark. The Principal Register of the US Patent and Trademark Office (&#147;USPTO&#148;) conveys the important substantive rights that most people associate with federal registration and, as a result, it is the preferred method of federal trademark protection. Probably the most important benefit of placing a mark on the Principal Register is that anybody who later initiates use of the same or a confusingly similar trademark may be presumed by the courts to be a &quot;willful infringer&quot; and therefore liable for damages. </P>

<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify><B><U>Product development</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>During its first five years, the Company&#146;s primary focus has been on product development. &nbsp;The Company&#146;s first product, a surface disinfectant called &#147;Viralex&#148; and subsequently renamed &#147;T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174; </SUP>Disinfectant&#148;, was launched in September of 2001. It is being sold primarily to (i) &#147;First Responder&#148; organizations including ambulance, fire fighters and police forces in Canada, (ii) dental clinics, and (iii) beauty and hair care salons and spas. T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174; </SUP>Disinfectant has been approved by Health Canada for use on any hard, inanimate non-porous surfaces. &nbsp;This includes, but is not limited to, counter tops, cutting boards, sinks, tubs, walls, floors, windows, mirrors, scissors, nail clippers and other equipment used in beauty salons and spas, dental mirrors and other equipment in dental offices, and equipment used by firefighters, police and paramedics. T<SUP>3</SUP
>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP> Disinfectant is also approved by the Canadian Food Inspection Agency (&#147;CFIA&#148;) for use in restaurants and other facilities where food is prepared.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:6.667px; padding-left:4.933px">Efficacy studies</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:6.667px; padding-left:4.933px">Efficacy studies refer to proving a drug's effectiveness (in this case as a disinfectant) in producing a desired result (bactericide, virucide, fungicide or tuberculocide). In studies conducted by independent laboratories in Canada and the United States, T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174; </SUP>Disinfectant has demonstrated efficacy against bacteria, fungi and viruses. The types of surfaces tested were hard non-porous surfaces unless otherwise noted.</P>
<P style="line-height:10pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-13.333px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:-24px; font-size:8pt">1.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:6.667px; padding-left:24px">An efficacy study, dated February 10, 1997, was conducted by British Columbia Research Inc. (Vancouver, Canada) under the supervision of Dr. Ernie Lee. The &nbsp;organisms tested were four strains of bacteria (<I>Staphylococcus epidermis, Pseudomonas aeruginosa, Serratia marcescens, and Mycobacterium tuberculosis)</I> one strain of yeast (<I>Candida albicans)</I>, spores from one strain of fungus (<I>Aspergillus fumigatus)</I> and two strains of viruses (<I>Herpes Simplex Virus-1 and Poliovirus-1)</I> in compliance with test standards accepted by Health Canada&#146;s Therapeutic Product Directorate Twenty five replicates of each organism at low levels, ranging from 38 to 177 cfu&#146;s/ml (colony forming units/ml) were dried on microscope cover slips and exposed to T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP> Disinfectant for varying times. The studies demonstrated that no growth occurred for any of the replicates. It was concluded that T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SU
P>&#174;</SUP> Disinfectant was 100% effective against all five organisms after 10 minutes or longer contact times. At shorter contact times, the kill rate for all 5 organisms ranged from 95.5% to 97.2% after a 1 minute exposure and 98.7 and 99.0% after a 5 minute exposure.</P>
<P style="line-height:10pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-13.333px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:-24px; font-size:8pt">2.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:6.667px; padding-left:24px">An efficacy study, dated June 6, 1997, was conducted by Dr. Richard Stokes of the University of British Columbia in conjunction with the British Columbia Children&#146;s Hospital. &nbsp;Twenty replicates of <I>Mycobacterium tuberculosis</I> at approximately 10<SUP>7</SUP>cfu&#146;s/ml were dried on microscope cover slips and exposed to T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP> Disinfectant for varying times. The studies demonstrated that the kill rate was 99.99997% (a reduction of log<SUB>10</SUB> = 6.46) and 99.99998% (a reduction of log<SUB>10</SUB> = 6.59) &nbsp;after a 10 minute exposure. The requirement for a disinfectant to be designated as &#147;Tuberculocidal&#148; by Health Canada is a log<SUB>10 </SUB>reduction of 6.0 or greater.</P>
<P style="line-height:10pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-13.333px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:-24px; font-size:8pt">3.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:6.667px; padding-left:24px">Efficacy studies were conducted by Viromed Biosafety Laboratories of Minneapolis, Minnesota, completed on February 23, 2000. The organisms tested were <I>Staphylococcus aureus, Pseumomonas aeruginosa, Salmonella choleraesuis</I>, Human Immunodeficiency Virus Type I, <I>Herpes simplex</I> Virus Type 1, <I>Trichophyton mentagrophytes </I>and <I>Poliovirus</I> Type 1, in compliance with test standards accepted by the Environmental Protection Agency (&#147;EPA&#148;) of the United States.</P>
