<P style="margin:0px; padding-bottom:4px; border-bottom:1px solid #000000" align=center><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify><B>Risks Pertaining to the Industry:</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify><B><I>Registration of products may not occur in a timely manner which could lead to delays in product introductions, reduced revenue expectations and extra costs to conduct further tests to satisfy regulatory agencies.</I></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>Government agencies, such as the EPA and the Food and Drug Administration (&#147;FDA&#148;) in the United States and Health Products and Food Branch in Canada, need to provide approvals of the Company&#146;s products prior to any sales of these products. &nbsp;To obtain such approvals, the Company must submit extensive amounts of information on the efficacy, toxicology, carcinogenicity, mutagenecity and other testing of the products that it is trying to register. After all of the information is provided, the agencies can request supplemental information and further testing. Once all of the requirement for documentation is satisfied, the agencies can take 24 months or longer to provide approvals for the Company to market its products. &nbsp;Significant delays could lead to slower revenue growth than anticipated. &nbsp;In addition, regulatory delays can allow time for competitors to devise strategies to prevent or reduce market penetration. &nbsp;There 
is no assurance that government agencies will accept for registration any of the Company&#146;s products.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify><B><I>There is a risk that the Company&#146;s intellectual property infringes upon the rights of other companies, which could lead to reduced revenues, reduced margins due to sanctions against the Company, outright withdrawal or prohibition of products or trademarks &nbsp;from the market and significant costs for legal defense against infringement claims, re-branding of products and revised marketing materials. &nbsp;</I></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>The Company is unaware of any infringement claims being made against the Company or its products or processes, except that JohnsonDiversey, Inc. (&#147;JDI&#148;) took action against the Company for use of the trademark, &#147;Viralex&#148;, which JDI claimed infringed on their trademark, Virex. &nbsp;This action was settled by the Company accepting a one-time payment of US$30,000 and agreeing to cease to use the name. &nbsp;The Company instead now uses the trademark &#147;T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP>&#148; for its products and this trademark is registered in both Canada and the US. The change of name from Viralex to T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174; </SUP>caused some confusion among the customers of the Company and required additional expenditures to be made for new labels, packaging and marketing materials, as well as mailings to advise customers of the change. There was no noticeable effect on overall sales on a quarterly basis beyond normal fluctuation
s. There can be no assurances that other third parties will not assert infringement claims in the future or require the Company to obtain a license for the intellectual property rights of such third parties. &nbsp;There can be no assurance that such a license, if required, will be available on reasonable terms or at all. &nbsp;If the Company does not obtain such a license, it could encounter delays in the introduction of products or could find that the development, manufacture or sale of products requiring such a license could be prohibited.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify><B><I>There is a risk that earlier inventions</I></B><I> </I><B><I>may exist that invalidate the Company&#146;s patent applications so that the Company may not be able to sell any infringing products.</I></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>Since patent applications are maintained in secrecy for a period of time after filing, and since publication of discoveries in the scientific or patent literature often lags behind actual discoveries, the Company cannot be certain that it was the first creator of inventions covered by pending patent applications, or that it was the first to file patent applications for such inventions. The Company might have to participate in interference proceedings in the U.S. Patent and Trademark Office to determine priority of invention, at substantial cost. There can be no assurance that the Company&#146;s patents, if issued, would be held valid or enforceable by a court. The Company has patents allowed in the United States, China and Australia and patent applications filed in the European Union, Canada, and Singapore. These patent applications seek intellectual property protection for the basic formulation of the T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174; </SUP>formulation and t
he method for making it.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify><B><I>There may be limited ability to defend the patents if and when they are issued, leading to loss of sales that might otherwise be realized if the Company was in a position to defend its patents.</I></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>Litigation among pharmaceutical companies can be intense and costly. &nbsp;The Company might not have the financial ability to defend its patents, if issued, against larger industry players. &nbsp;Litigation may be necessary to enforce patents issued or assigned to the Company, or to determine the scope and validity of a third party's proprietary rights. &nbsp;Additionally, there can be no assurances that the Company would prevail in any such action. &nbsp;An adverse outcome in litigation or as part of an interference or other proceeding in a court or patent office could subject the Company to significant liabilities, require disputed rights to be licensed from other parties or require the Company to cease using certain technology or products, any of which could have a material adverse effect on the Company&#146;s business.</P>

<P style="margin:0px" align=center>MANAGEMENT DISCUSSION AND ANALYSIS (&#147;MD&amp;A&#148;)</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center>FOR THE THREE MONTH PERIOD ENDED SEPTEMBER 30, 2008</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-bottom:4px; border-bottom:1px solid #000000" align=center><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify><B><U>Risk Factors (continued)</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify><B><I>The market for disinfectant products is competitive and well established with a number of large, multinational, widely recognized companies with significant financial and marketing resources selling, and possibly developing, similar products. </I></B>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>Competitors are already well established in the market for disinfectant products. &nbsp;The introduction of a new product into this existing market could be met with aggressive marketing, price cutting and distribution impediments by competitors. &nbsp;To obtain market share, the Company&#146;s business must penetrate a market with established competitors and obtain sufficient recognition to be able to displace the existing disinfectant products. &nbsp;Substantial funds will have to be spent on marketing and education to achieve these objectives. &nbsp;Competitors may be developing new technologies and new products that will offer significant improvements over existing products, including those offered by the Company. There can be no assurance that others will not independently develop similar products, duplicate any of the Company&#146;s products or, if patents are issued to the Company, design around such patents. &nbsp;There can be no assurance tha
t a competitor's technology or product would be found to infringe the Company&#146;s patents. Key competitors are Germiphene Corporation, Virox Technologies, Inc., JohnsonDiversey Inc., Advanced Sterilization Products and Metrex Research Corporation. All of these companies are well established and sell disinfection products into the same markets served by the Company. </P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify><B><I>The Company&#146;s T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP> Disinfectant is composed of various chemicals that may pose risks due to flammability and possible health risks.</I></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:5.533px; margin-bottom:5.533px">One of the main components of T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP> Disinfectant is ethanol, which is flammable and has a flash point (the minimum temperature at which the liquid produces a sufficient concentration of vapour above it that it forms an ignitable mixture with air) of 13 <SUP>o</SUP>C. Bitrex, which is added to ethanol as a denaturant to prevent the consumption of the ethanol, is also a fire retardant and raises the flash point of T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP> Disinfectant to 24<SUP>o</SUP>C. The transport and storage of T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP> Disinfectant can pose a fire hazard if shipped or stored in sufficient quantities. The Company uses an independent warehousing company to store and ship T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP> Disinfectant. The warehouse is fully equipped with fire suppression equipment according to the relevant regulations established by the municipal, provincial and federal governments. T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP> Dis
infectant is shipped by ground only in cases of 4 bottles holding 4 litres each or 12 bottles holding 0.48 litres. In these quantities, T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP> Disinfectant is not classified as a &#147;Dangerous Good&#148; under Sections 1.15, 1.16 and 1.17 of the &#147;Transportation of Dangerous Goods Act&#148; administered by Transport Canada. As a result, no special regulations apply to the shipping of T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP> Disinfectant by ground within Canada. There is no guarantee that special shipping regulations will not be applied to shipments of T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP> Disinfectant in the future or in other jurisdictions, such as the United States.</P>
<P style="margin-top:5.533px; margin-bottom:5.533px">Two potentially toxic components of T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP> Disinfectant are present in low concentrations compared to their LD<SUB>50</SUB> levels (the amount of the substance that kills 50% of the test population of experimental animals when administered as a single dose). O-phenylphenol (&#147;OPP&#148;) in pure crystalline form is considered to be a possible carcinogen and eye contact can cause severe irritation or burns with possible eye damage (Concentration in T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP> Disinfectant = 2,800 ppm, oral LD<SUB>50</SUB> = 2,480 mg/kg in rats) For some individuals, o-phenylphenol can also irritate the skin. Benzalkonium chloride (BZK) supplied as a 50% solution in water, has been reported to cause allergic reactions and the swelling of the mucosa when used as nose sprays on a continuous, long-term basis by sensitive users (Concentration in T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP> Disinfectant = 2,000 ppm, oral LD<SUB>50</SUB> = 300 m
g/kg in rats). The Company does not directly handle, store, use or dispose of OPP or BZK in pure form but only in their highly diluted form in T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP> Disinfectant. Further, because the denatured alcohol that contains Bitrex to prepare T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP> Disinfectant, the consumption of significant amounts of T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP> Disinfectant is not possible. Therefore, it is highly unlikely that anyone can be poisoned or otherwise harmed through the proper use of T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP> Disinfectant as instructed by the Company.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><BR>
<BR></P>
</DIV><DIV style="width:600px"><P style="line-height:10pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-13.333px; font-size:8pt">ALDA 2008-03-30 Q1 MD&amp;A</P>
<P style="line-height:10pt; margin:0px; text-indent:549.933px; font-size:8pt">Page 22<BR>
- ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin:0px; text-indent:568px; font-size:12pt; page-break-before:always">&nbsp;&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
</DIV><DIV style="width:624px"><P style="margin:0px" align=center><B>ALDA PHARMACEUTICALS CORP</B>.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center>MANAGEMENT DISCUSSION AND ANALYSIS (&#147;MD&amp;A&#148;)</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center>FOR THE THREE MONTH PERIOD ENDED SEPTEMBER 30, 2008</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-bottom:4px; border-bottom:1px solid #000000" align=center><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><B><U>Risk Factors (continued)</U></B></P>
<P style="margin-top:5.533px; margin-bottom:5.533px">Toxicology studies conducted for the company by Product Safety Labs (&#147;PSL&#148;), located in Dayton, New Jersey, have confirmed &nbsp;that T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP> Disinfectant has no harmful effects on animals except as reported below by PSL:</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:-24px; font-family:Symbol">&#183;</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px">Acute inhalation (rat): LC<SUB>50</SUB> &gt; 2020 mg/m3. Difficulty breathing, irregular respiration, lethargy and discharge from nose and eyes reported.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:-24px; font-family:Symbol">&#183;</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px">Acute oral (rat): LD<SUB>50</SUB> &gt; 5000 mg/kg. Lethargy and hunched posture reported.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:-24px; font-family:Symbol">&#183;</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px">Acute dermal (rat): LD<SUB>50</SUB> &gt; 2000 mg/kg. No systemic effects observed.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:-24px; font-family:Symbol">&#183;</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px">Effects not observed but possible based on individual ingredients may include: ataxia, loss of coordination, drowsiness, intoxication, nausea and vomiting.</P>
<P style="margin:0px">However, T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP> Disinfectant &nbsp;is classified as a moderate eye irritant. &nbsp;Although T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP> Disinfectant is not measurably toxic if used as directed, it is possible that regulations against these chemicals may become more restrictive and affect the ability of the Company to market its products in certain jurisdictions without additional warning labels. None of the chemicals present in T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP> pose a serious threat to the environment and are biodegradable. &nbsp;However, given the attention that any chemicals may attract from environmental groups, it is possible that negative publicity about these chemicals could affect the ability of the company to market its products in certain jurisdictions. There are persuasive arguments and credible scientific evidence that is available to support the safety of T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP> Disinfectant, but such an educational effort on the part of the Company would 
require funds to be spent and would affect the profitability of the Company.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify><B><I>The Company has a limited number of customers and is dependent on a few key accounts to maintain its current levels of sales.</I></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>The key customers for which sales account for more than 10% of total revenues are:</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:-24px; font-family:Symbol" align=justify><U>&#183;</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px" align=justify><U>Esthetics Plus,&nbsp;Inc</U>.: A distributor to the beauty market&nbsp;with a contract that renews on an annual basis. Either party can terminate the contract on 60 days notice or with 30 days notice for any breach of the contract if the breach is not rectified within the 30 day notice period,</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:-24px; font-family:Symbol" align=justify><U>&#183;</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px" align=justify><U>Sinclair Dental Limited: </U>A distributor to the dental market and a customer of both API and the Company for 7 years,</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:-24px; font-family:Symbol" align=justify><U>&#183;</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px" align=justify><U>The Stevens Company Limited</U>: A distributor to the scientific and medical markets and a customer of both API and the Company for 7 years, and</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:-24px; font-family:Symbol" align=justify><U>&#183;</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px" align=justify><U>VWR International</U>: A distributor to the laboratory market and customer of API and the Company for 7 years.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:-24px; font-family:Symbol">&#183;</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px">Product Distribution Centre: A distributor that is owned by the provincial government of BC, supplies the province&#146;s public sector consumers within BC and a customer of the Company and API for 7 years.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>The Company currently sells its T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP> Disinfectant through these distributors and is introducing new products, such as the T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP> Antiseptic Hand Sanitizer, T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP> &quot;Ready to Use&quot; Disinfectant Cleaner, T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP> Disinfectant Cleaner CONCENTRATE, and the corresponding wipes through these same distributors. The current sales and the plans to introduce the new products through these distributors would be disrupted if any of these distributors stopped representing the Company. The result would be a reduction in the Company&#146;s revenues until new distributors could be found. It is possible that new distributors could not be found and the Company would have to try to sell its products directly to the end users, leading to a significant increase in marketing and sales costs even if the sales levels could be regained.</P>

</DIV><DIV style="width:624px"><P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><B>ALDA PHARMACEUTICALS CORP</B>.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center>MANAGEMENT DISCUSSION AND ANALYSIS (&#147;MD&amp;A&#148;)</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center>FOR THE THREE MONTH PERIOD ENDED SEPTEMBER 30, 2008</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-bottom:4px; border-bottom:1px solid #000000" align=center><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px"><B>1.3 </B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:14px; text-indent:37.8px"><B>SELECTED FINANCIAL INFORMATION (continued)</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>As of September 30, 2008, the Company had a cash position of $2,207,854 due to the completion of a private placements undertaken in prior year and from exercising of warrants and options. The funds were designated for use as working capital and for general and administrative purposes. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>The current assets were $2,337,124 while current liabilities were $52,718. The Company recognized a net loss of $263,864 from operations for the three months period ended September 30, 2008 due to increases in consulting fees paid to the consultants that were engaged to assist with regulatory submissions to the FDA and Health Canada. Non-cash stock-based compensation expenses were accounted for $39,542. &nbsp;Revenues of $55,537 were generated from the sale of T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174; </SUP>Disinfectant and T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174; </SUP>Hand Sanitizer to the dental, beauty and first responder markets. &nbsp;The revenues were relatively consistent from period to period and are not yet significant compared to the costs incurred by the Company at this stage of its development. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify><B>Overview</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>Over the course of the Company&#146;s operating history, the Company has successfully secured the required government and regulatory approvals to market and sell its T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174; </SUP>Disinfectant products in Canada. &nbsp;This has resulted in sales as described in Results of Operations below. To date, all of the Company&#146;s sales have been in Canada which, while a developed industrial economy, is not a particularly large market relative to economies such as the United States or China. To achieve profitability and increase sales substantially, the Company must first secure government and regulatory approval of its products in markets outside of Canada or secure registrations for additional products within Canada. Although sales in Canada have been consistent over the Company&#146;s operating history, the Company has not yet secured the required government and regulatory approvals for the sales of its products outside of Canada except 
in China through the efforts of the Company&#146;s agent in China. &nbsp;Each government or regulatory jurisdiction tends to require efficacy studies or safety studies of differing content or quality. &nbsp;The regulatory approval process to date has been costly both in terms of working capital and in terms of management time and attention.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>The Company has been actively marketing its T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174; </SUP>Disinfectant product since the acquisition of API was completed. A standard alcohol hand sanitizer is also manufactured for the Company by Norwood Packaging.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>The Company&#146;s sales show no significant variation from quarter to quarter. The Company&#146;s sales during the three month period ended September 30, 2008, and the last two corresponding quarter ended September 30, 2006 and 2005 were $55,660, $55,537 and $57,575, respectively. The unit cost of sales has also stabilized as a percentage of sales in the same corresponding quarters. &nbsp;However, the Company is still operating overall with a significant loss from operations. &nbsp;This reflects, to a great extent, the costs associated with the work being done to register its products for sale in jurisdictions other than Canada and ongoing administrative, management and intellectual property protection costs. To generate a net profit, the Company believes that it must register its products for sale in another major market, such as the United States or China or both, to achieve sales economies or achieve significant sales of its newer products such as
 the hand sanitizer and disinfectant cleaners. However, even if the Company becomes operationally profitable from the introduction and sale of new products, the Company plans to invest heavily in clinical testing and registration of its therapeutic products in Canada, the EU and the US through Health Canada, the EMA and the FDA, respectively. To accomplish these goals, the Company will need to raise significant amounts of new funding and the expenses associated with these activities will affect the ability of the Company to show a profit until they are completed.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>

</DIV><DIV style="width:624px"><P style="margin:0px; padding-left:9.467px; padding-right:-7.6px" align=center><B>ALDA PHARMACEUTICALS CORP.</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center>MANAGEMENT DISCUSSION AND ANALYSIS (&#147;MD&amp;A&#148;)</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center>FOR THE THREE MONTH PERIOD ENDED SEPTEMBER 30, 2008</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-bottom:4px; border-bottom:1px solid #000000" align=center><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:37.933px; text-indent:-33px" align=justify><B>1.3</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:37.933px" align=justify><B>SELECTED FINANCIAL INFORMATION (continued)</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify><B>Trend information</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>There are no markets or other trends which the Company believes materially affect its business prospects other than small seasonal dips in sales observed during the summer months and over Christmas and into the New Year. The Company&#146;s existing customers and the general public are becoming more aware of disinfectant products. The continuing spread of antibiotic-resistant bacteria is contributing to this awareness and a perception that there is a growing need or demand for products similar to those the Company produces. This has resulted in growth in the market for disinfectant products, in particular consumer products which provide antibacterial soaps and lotions. &nbsp;No reliable quantification of the growth these product sales have experienced is available and no growth or future growth can be reliably predicted. The Company believes that its revenues will increase as new products, based on the T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174; </SUP>formulation are la
unched.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:37.933px; text-indent:-33px" align=justify><B>1.4</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:37.933px" align=justify><B>&nbsp;RESULTS OF OPERATIONS </B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify><B>Sales</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>As the T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP> Disinfectant Cleaner Concentrate and T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP> Antiseptic Hand Sanitizer are still pending, &nbsp;the Company&#146;s sales were primarily due to the sale of T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174; </SUP>Disinfectant and T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174; </SUP>Hand Sanitizer through its distributors to the first responders, dental and beauty markets. The Company recorded sales of $55,660 for the three month period ended September 30, 2008 as compared to $55,537 for the three month period ended September 30, 2007. The Company relies heavily on its current distributors to provide T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174; </SUP>products to customers. </P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>The Company anticipates that the sales will grow when more products, including T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP> Antiseptic Hand Sanitizer Gel, , and T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP> Disinfectant Cleaner Concentrate, are introduced to the market. The Company observed that no new major competitors have appeared in the market nor have any withdrawn from the market. However, certain companies have introduced new varieties of disinfectant products, including disinfectant products in wipe form to the market so that the selection of products appears to be increasing.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify><B>Cost of Sales</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>For the three month period ended September 30, 2008, the cost of sales incurred was $37,870, representing 68% of total sales as compared to $35,679, representing 64% of total sales for the same corresponding period of last fiscal year. &nbsp;As anticipated, the cost of sales increased due to an increase in warehousing costs and handling charges. Cost of sales includes the direct costs of the inventory sold during the period plus warehousing costs, shipping and handling charges. </P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify><B>Gross Profit</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>For the three month period ended September 30, 2008, &nbsp;the Company recorded a gross profit of $17,790. &nbsp;A gross profit of $19,858 was recognized in same corresponding quarter of last fiscal year. Gross profit has been remained relatively stable over the reported periods.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify><B>Advertising and Promotion</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>Advertising and promotion costs for the three month period ended September 30, 2008 and 2007 were $1,201 and $6,479, respectively. The Company did not undertake any promotion with the distributers. &nbsp;The Company anticipates that additional investment in this area is required in subsequent quarters when the new products, such as T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP> Antiseptic Hand Sanitizer Gel, and T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP> Disinfectant Cleaner Concentrate, are introduced to the current distributors and to the market. &nbsp;New promotional literature will be provided to the current and new distributors. </P>

<P style="margin:0px" align=center>MANAGEMENT DISCUSSION AND ANALYSIS (&#147;MD&amp;A&#148;)</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center>FOR THE THREE MONTH PERIOD ENDED SEPTEMBER 30, 2008</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-bottom:4px; border-bottom:1px solid #000000" align=center><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify><B>1.4 &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;RESULTS OF OPERATIONS (continued)</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify><B>Consulting</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>Consulting fees for the three months period ended September 30 2008 and 2007 were $114,458 and $75,330, respectively. &nbsp;An increase of $39,128 over the corresponding quarters was primarily due to the non-cash compensation expenses of $39,542 being recognized in consulting fees as described in Note 7(b) of the interim consolidated financial statements. Included in the consulting fees were $81,000 paid to executives of the Company in remuneration for their services to the Company. &nbsp;The related party transactions were provided in Note 9 of the interim consolidated financial statements. &nbsp;The Company hired third party consultants to carry out ongoing projects including branding, marketing and product development.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify><B>Investor Relations</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify>The investor relations activities amounted to $44,025and $21,344 for the three month period ended September 30, 2008 and 2007, respectively. &nbsp;Freeform Communications, Inc. (&#147;Freeform&#148;) provided their services to the Company and in return, the Company paid a total of $12,000 &nbsp;and $10,000 for the three month period ended September 30, 2008 and 2007, respectively, to Freeform. &nbsp;Included in this category was a portion of the non-cash stock-based compensation of $31,338 for options provided to Freeform and fees of $687 paid to Marketwire for the three month period ended September 30, 2008 for the dissemination of news releases. &nbsp;The Company paid $1,344 to Marketwire for the same corresponding quarter of last year. </P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify><B>Legal and Accounting Fees</B></P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px" align=justify>Legal and accounting fees were totaled $15,268 and $10,407 for the three month period ended September 30, 2008 and 2007, respectively. &nbsp;An increase in legal and accounting fees was partly due to the ongoing foreign securities registration assisted by Stanislaw Ashbaugh L.L.P. &nbsp;Legal fees incurred in the periods consisted of advising the Company on general legal matters, attending to preparation of required and revised documentation to the TSX Venture Exchange and the securities commissions and reviewing 20F documents for the registration of the Company&#146;s securities in the United States. Accounting fees consisted of the additional cost of the audits. </P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify><B>Product Registration and Development Costs</B></P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px" align=justify>Total costs incurred in this category for the three month period ended September 30, 2008 and 2007 were $65,317 and $5,898, respectively. &nbsp;The expenses related to development activities, which do not meet generally accepted criteria for deferral, and research activities are expensed as incurred.. Costs incurred in the quarter included testing fees paid to BioScience Laboratories, Inc. to undertake clinical testing for the T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP> therapeutic applications, and consultants fees paid to regulatory consultants in Canada and US to pursue the registration of the Company&#146;s therapeutic products.</P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px; padding-right:-7.6px" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify><B>Wages and Benefits</B></P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px" align=justify>Wages and benefits were increased to $16,988 for the three month period ended September 30, 2008 as compared to &nbsp;$12,853 for the three month period ended September 30, 2007. &nbsp;Costs in this category include the wages paid to accounting and administrative assistance and to sales and marketing staff. &nbsp;</P>

<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify><B>Loss from Operations</B></P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px" align=justify>The loss from operations was $266,877 for the three month period ended September 30, 2008 as compared to $136,074 for same corresponding quarter of last fiscal year. &nbsp;Losses for the quarter ended September 30, 2008 were significantly greater due to the non-cash stock based compensation expenses of $39,542 being recognized in the statement of operations. The Company recorded no stock based compensation in the same corresponding quarter of last fiscal year. The Company continued to have Dr. Hibbard assist with regulatory matters to satisfy FDA&#146;s requirements and to evaluate the potential applications and development of the Company&#146;s T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP> technology and the regulatory pathways to commercialization and PharmEng Technology to assist regulatory matters in Canada and EU. The Company continued to pursue the registration of its securities in the US with the assistance of Stanis
law &amp; Ashbaugh, LLP. </P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px" align=justify>Management continues to work towards the launch of new products, including T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174; </SUP>Disinfex Disinfectant Spray, T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174; </SUP>Antiseptic Hand Sanitizer, T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP> Disinfectant Cleaner Concentrate, T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174;</SUP> Disinfectant Cleaner Wipes and the therapeutic products. The pursuit of the new therapeutics products requires the Company to invest continuously in product development, clinical trials, product registrations and intellectual property protection. &nbsp;As a result, further losses will be anticipated in subsequent years. </P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-right:4.933px" align=justify><B>&nbsp;Other Income (Loss)</B></P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px" align=justify>Interest income earned from bank deposits for the three month period ended September 30, 2008 and 2007 was $3,013 and $4,990, respectively. &nbsp;The increase was due to an increase in cash position upon the closing of various private placements and the exercising of options and warrants from the holders during 2008 fiscal year.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px" align=justify><B>Loss for the Year</B></P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px" align=justify>The interest income earned over the quarter reduced the loss for the three month period ended September 30, 2008 to $263,864, &nbsp;as compared to $131,084 in the same corresponding fiscal year last year. &nbsp;&nbsp;The non-cash compensation expenses of $39,542 and $nil were being in the statement of operations for the three month period ended September 30, 2008 and 2007, respectively. The details of non-cash compensation were disclosed in Note 7(b) of the interim consolidated financial statements. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>

<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:14px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:4.933px"><B>1.5 &nbsp;&nbsp;SUMMARY OF QUARTERLY RESULTS (continued)</B></P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px; padding-right:-7.6px" align=justify>The revenues generated from the sale of T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174; </SUP>Disinfectant and T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174; </SUP>Hand Sanitizer have been relatively consistent for the three month period ended September 30, 2008 and the last two corresponding quarter ended September 30, 2007 and 2006. The revenues were ranging from $55,000 to $73,000 per quarter. &nbsp;The difference is attributable to the timing of ordering and some seasonality as described above. &nbsp;&nbsp;Cost of goods was also very consistent over the periods reported. Operating expenses vary from quarter to quarter depending on the activities taking place such as registering T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174; </SUP>products in major markets, pursuing clinical trials, seeking expert advice on product regulatory issues, re-branding and advertising current and new lines of products and seeking registration of ALDA&#146;s securities in the US. &nbsp;Greater losses were incurred i
n the second and fourth quarters of 2008 due to the non-cash stock-based compensation expenses of $478,238 and $402,057 accounted for in the fourth and second quarter of 2008, respectively, and the impairment loss of $190,638 on patent application and development costs and intangible assets. For the three month period ended September 30, 2008, the non-cash stock-based compensation expenses were $39,542. &nbsp;In connection with the settlement of legal disputes, the Company recognized a net gain of $10,545 in fiscal year 2007. &nbsp;As described in Section 1.2 &#147;Overall Performance of the Company&#148;, the Company continued to observe net losses. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px" align=justify>Total assets increased significantly over the reported periods as a result of closing private placements and exercising of options and warrants. &nbsp;The total assets, as of September 30, 2008, were $2,342,449. The cash and equivalents representing 94% of the total assets while accounts payable and accruals were $52,718. For the last corresponding quarter ended September 30, 2007, the Company had total assets of $1,255,681; cash and equivalents accounted for 74% of the total assets.. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin-top:4px; margin-bottom:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4px; padding-right:4.933px"><B>1.6 &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;LIQUIDITY</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px" align=justify>Although the Company generates some revenues from the sale of its lead product, T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174; </SUP>Disinfectant, sales are mainly occurring in Canada and commencing in China. &nbsp;T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174; </SUP>Disinfectant is registered in the United Kingdom and the Company will be pursuing opportunities in European markets but no firm plan has yet been established. &nbsp;The manufacturing facility for the Company&#146;s products in China is now in operation. &nbsp;The Company has also established a plan for the development, testing, registration and marketing of therapeutic applications of the T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174; </SUP>formulation. &nbsp;Management is also evaluating the possibility of acquiring technologies that are complementary to T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174; </SUP>technology and launching similar type of products lines in the near future. &nbsp;It is expected that the Company will need 
to undertake further financing in order to pursue these plans and these financings will lead to the dilution of current shareholders of the Company. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin-top:4px; margin-bottom:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:28.933px; padding-right:4.933px; text-indent:-24px"><B>1.7</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:28.933px; padding-right:4.933px"><B>&nbsp;CAPITAL RESOURCES </B></P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px" align=justify>During the three month period ended September 30, 2008, the Company received $38,000 from the exercise of 380,000 options at an exercise price range of $0.10 per option. &nbsp;Option values of $7,600 previously recorded in contributed previously recorded in contributed surplus for options were credited to share capital. &nbsp;106,250 options granted on December 7, 2007 at an exercise price of $0.50 and 25,000 options granted on May 2, 2008 at an exercise price of $0.80 were vested with option values of $39,542 recorded in contributed surplus for options.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px" align=justify>As at September 30, 2008, the Company had 49,891,799 outstanding common shares and a total of 6,677,500 outstanding warrants exercisable at an exercise price range of $0.24 to $0.45 before the date of expiration. The outstanding stock options as at September 30, 2008 &nbsp;were 4,420,000 (4,113,750 options exercisable) at an exercise price range of $0.11 to $0.80 per option. &nbsp;Upon the exercise of outstanding warrants and options, the Company will have fully diluted outstanding common shares of 60,551,799. &nbsp;</P>

<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px; padding-left:34.933px; padding-right:-7.6px" align=justify><B>CAPITAL RESOURCES (continued)</B></P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px" align=justify>At the time of this report, the Company has sufficient working capital to pursue its development plans and to fund its operations. &nbsp;However, there can be no guarantee that the Company will derive any proceeds from the exercise of outstanding warrants and options. &nbsp;There is no assurance that additional funding will be made available to the Company to fulfill its business objectives. &nbsp;In additional there can be no assurance that the Company will be able to obtain adequate financing in the future to fulfill its business objectives or that the terms of such financing will be favourable. &nbsp;Many of the Company&#146;s products still require further development, laboratory testing and human testing in order to obtain required regulatory approvals. &nbsp;A lack of funds will impair the ability of the Company to complete such tests. &nbsp;A lack of funds will also impair the Company&#146;s ability to 
establish marketing and sales plans once the products have been approved for sale. &nbsp;If adequate financing is not available when required, the Company may be required to delay, scale back or eliminate various activities and may be unable to continue in operation. &nbsp;The Company may seek such additional financing through debt or equity offerings, which might alter the capital structure of the Company, but there can be no assurance that such financing will be available on terms acceptable to the Company or at all. &nbsp;Any equity offering will result in dilution to the ownership interests of the Company&#146;s shareholders and may result in dilution to the value of such interests.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><B>1.8 &nbsp;&nbsp;COMMITMENTS AND AGREEMENTS </B></P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:14.6pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-19.467px; padding-left:28.8px; padding-right:-7.667px; text-indent:-28.8px" align=justify>a)</P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:6.667px; padding-left:28.8px; padding-right:-7.667px" align=justify>Effective January 1, 2006, the Company entered into an agreement to lease its office premises over a period of one year. &nbsp;After the first year, a holding over provision is instituted in which the landlord accepts rent from the Company, the new tenancy is a month to month tenancy, subject to the terms and covenants of the lease which are applicable to a month to month tenancy, except that:</P>
<P style="line-height:14.6pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-19.467px; padding-left:48px; padding-right:-7.667px; text-indent:-19.2px" align=justify>(1)</P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:3.333px; padding-left:48px; padding-right:-7.667px" align=justify>it will be subject to termination by the Landlord on one week's written notice to the Tenant;</P>
<P style="line-height:14.6pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-19.467px; padding-left:48px; padding-right:-7.667px; text-indent:-19.2px" align=justify>(2)</P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:3.333px; padding-left:48px; padding-right:-7.667px" align=justify>there will be no right of renewal; and</P>
<P style="line-height:14.6pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-19.467px; padding-left:48px; padding-right:-7.667px; text-indent:-19.2px" align=justify>(3)</P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:3.333px; padding-left:48px; padding-right:-7.667px" align=justify>the monthly Basic Rent payable will be increased by 50% above the monthly basic rent last payable under the &nbsp;lease. This condition has not been imposed on the Company by the landlord because the space has been subjected to an extended period of renovation, the rented area has been has changed and the landlord is a company controlled by a director of the Company.</P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px; padding-left:28.4px; padding-right:-7.6px" align=justify>The Company&#146;s minimum lease payment obligations under the agreement as at July 1, 2008, totaled $26,320, payable in the 2009 fiscal year.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:14.6pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-19.467px; padding-left:28.4px; padding-right:-7.6px; text-indent:-28.4px" align=justify>b)</P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px; padding-left:28.4px; padding-right:-7.6px" align=justify>The Agreement with Fuzhou Xinmei Biotech Co. Ltd. (&#147;Fuzhou&#148;), which allowed manufacturing and marketing in Fujian province in China, was transferred to He-Yi She Ye Limited (&#147;He-Yi&#148;) and expanded to cover marketing in all of China. Prior to that transfer of rights, the agent for Fuzhou secured a Certificate of Approval, on August 31, 2006, from the Fujian Centre of Disease Control for T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174; </SUP>Disinfectant after passing all of the required tests. This certificate allowed the agent for Fuzhou to apply to the Chinese National Centre for Health Inspection and Supervision for approval to manufacture T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174; </SUP>Disinfectant for sale in China and for export. The registration of T<SUP>3</SUP>6<SUP>&#174; </SUP>Disinfectant in China was expanded beyond disinfection of inanimate objects, such as hospital equipment and instruments, to also allow external use
 on humans, including use as a first-aid antiseptic and hand sanitizer. &nbsp;He-Yi has provided a fully equipped manufacturing facility according to the specifications provided by ALDA, to produce the ALDA products. He-Yi will have the right to distribute ALDA&#146;s products in China subject to ALDA&#146;s approval of each distributorship.</P>

<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:4.933px"><B>1.13 &nbsp;&nbsp;CRITICAL ACCOUNTING ESTIMATES </B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px" align=justify>The preparation of the financial statements in conformity with Canadian GAAP requires management to make estimates and assumptions that affect the amounts reported of assets and liabilities, the disclosure of contingent assets and liabilities at the date of financial statements and the amounts of revenues and expenses for the reporting period. &nbsp;The areas of estimation are the stock-based compensation, estimated useful lives of depreciable assets, and intellectual property. &nbsp;The Company believes that the estimates and assumptions upon which it relies are reasonable and are based on information available to the Company at the time that estimates and assumptions are made. &nbsp;Actual results could differ from those estimates. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:4.933px"><B>1.14a &nbsp;&nbsp;CHANGES IN ACCOUNTING POLICIES INCLUDING INITIAL ADOPTION </B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px" align=justify>Effective July 1, 2001, the Company adopted the new recommendations of the Canadian Institute of Chartered Accountants Accounting Handbook Section 3870, Stock-based Compensation and Other Stock-based Payments (&quot;CICA 3870&quot;). During the year ended June 30, 2004, CICA 3870 was amended to require the use of the fair value-based method to account for stock Options granted to employees. In accordance with the revised recommendations, the Company has prospectively applied the fair value-based method to all stock Options granted to employees on or after July 1, 2003, whereby compensation cost is measured at fair value at the date of grant and is expensed over the vesting period.</P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px" align=justify>Effective July 1, 2003, the Company adopted the recommendations of the Canadian Institute of Chartered Accountants Handbook, Section 3063, Impairment of long-lived assets (&quot;CICA 3063&quot;). The new recommendations were applied prospectively to all long-lived assets held for use by the Company after July 1, 2003.</P>

<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px" align=justify><B>1.14a &nbsp;&nbsp;CHANGES IN ACCOUNTING POLICIES INCLUDING INITIAL ADOPTION (continued)</B></P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px" align=justify>The financial statements include a note providing reconciliation to United States Generally Accepted Accounting Standards (&#147;GAAS&#148;).</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px" align=justify>Patent application and development costs include all expenditures attributable to efforts by the Company to develop, and bring to commercial production a new product as well as to acquire legal protections for its proprietary products, such as trademarks and patents. &nbsp;Such amounts are charged as an expense in the period incurred except in circumstances where the market and technical feasibility of the product have been established, and recovery of patent application and development costs can reasonably be regarded as assured and future values can be realized, in which case such costs are capitalized. &nbsp;In the latter case, patent application and development costs are amortized on a systematic basis over the patent life of 20 years. &nbsp;&nbsp;The carrying amounts of intangible assets which are determined to have a finite useful life are amortized on a systematic basis over the useful life of 20 years.
 At this time, no patent costs or intangible assets are capitalized.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px" align=justify>The Company adopted the following new accounting standards issued by the Canadian Institute of Chartered Accountants (&#147;CICA&#148;) relating to comprehensive income, recognition, measurement, disclosure and presentation of financial instruments and hedges. &nbsp;These new accounting standards are applied prospectively beginning July 1, 2007. &nbsp;Adoption of these standards had no impact on the consolidated financial statements for the three month period ended September 30, 2008</P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px" align=justify>Section 1530 &#150; Comprehensive Income &#150; This section established standards for reporting and presentation of a statement of comprehensive income. &nbsp;Comprehensive income includes net earnings and other comprehensive income. &nbsp;Other comprehensive income is defined as the change in equity from transactions and other events from non owner sources. &nbsp;Other comprehensive income includes holding gains and losses on certain derivative instruments that are classified as available-for-sale, and gains or losses due to the change in foreign currency relating to self-sustaining foreign operations, all of which are not recognized in net earnings until realized. &nbsp;&nbsp;</P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px" align=justify>Section 3251 &#150; Equity &#150; In addition to Section 1530 (Comprehensive Income), this section establishes standards for the presentation of equity and changes in equity during the reporting period. </P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px" align=justify>Section 3855 &#150; Financial Instruments &#150; Recognition and Measurement &#150; This section established standards for recognizing and measuring financial instruments in the balance sheets and specifying how unrealized or realized gains and losses are to be presented during the reporting period. &nbsp;In accordance with the new accounting standard, all financial assets and financial liabilities are measured at fair value on initial recognition except for certain related party transaction.</P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px" align=justify>Financial instruments have been classified as held-to-maturity, available-for-sale, held for trading, loans and receivables, or other financial liabilities. &nbsp;Financial assets that are held to maturity, other than those held for trading, are measured at amortized cost. &nbsp;Available-for-sale instruments are measured at fair value with unrealized gains and losses recognized in other comprehensive income until realized, at which time realized gains and losses will be recognized in net income. &nbsp;Held for trading instruments are measured at fair value with unrealized gains and losses recognized in the results of operations in the period in which they arise. &nbsp;Loans and receivables are measured at amortized cost using the effective interest method. &nbsp;Any gains or losses on the realization of loans and receivables are included in earnings. &nbsp;Financial liabilities that are not classified as held
 to maturity are classified as other financial liabilities, and are carried at amortized costs using the effective interest method. &nbsp;Any gains and losses on realization of other financial liabilities are included in earnings. &nbsp;Any transaction costs incurred to acquire financial instruments will be included in earnings.</P>

<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px" align=justify>The Company&#146;s financial instruments consist of cash and equivalents, accounts receivable, prepaid expenses and others, subscriptions receivable, and accounts payable and accrued liabilities. &nbsp;The fair value of these instruments approximates the carrying amounts due to the immediate or short-term maturity of these financial instruments. The Company has made the following classifications:</P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:14.6pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-19.467px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px; text-indent:91.067px" align=justify>Cash and equivalents</P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px; text-indent:331.067px" align=justify>Held for trading</P>
<P style="line-height:14.6pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-19.467px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px; text-indent:91.067px" align=justify>Accounts receivable</P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px; text-indent:331.067px" align=justify>Loans and receivable</P>
<P style="line-height:14.6pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-19.467px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px; text-indent:91.067px" align=justify>Prepaids expenses and others</P>

<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px; text-indent:331.067px" align=justify>Other financial liabilities</P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px" align=justify>Section 3861 &#150; Financial Instruments &#150; Disclosure and Presentation &#150; This section establishes standards for presentation of financial instruments and non-financial derivates and identifies the information that should be disclosed about them. &nbsp;This section establishes standards for presentation of financial instruments and identifies the information which should be disclosed about them. &nbsp;Under the new standards, policies followed for years prior to the effective date are generally not reversed, and therefore the comparative figures have not been restated.</P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px" align=justify>Section 3862 &#150; Financial Instruments &#150; Disclosures and Section 3863 &#150; Financial Instruments &#150; Presentation - These sections revised and enhance the disclosure requirements while carrying forward its presentation requirements. &nbsp;These new sections will place increased emphasis on disclosures about the nature and extent of risks associated with both recognized and unrecognized financial instruments, how the entity manages the risks, and the exposure to liquidity, currency and other price risks.</P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px" align=justify>It is management&#146;s opinion that the Company is not exposed to significant interest, currency, credit, and liquidity risk arising from these financial instruments. &nbsp;The Company has transactions dominated in US dollars but exposure to currency risk is immaterial. &nbsp;The Company mitigates its exposure to credit risk by maintaining its primary operating accounts with chartered bank in Canada and constantly monitoring credit standing of counterparties. &nbsp;The Company manages its liquidity risk through the management of its capital as described in note 14. &nbsp;The Company does not use financial derivatives.</P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px" align=justify>Section 3865 &#150; Hedges &#150; This section establishes standards for the Company that chooses to designate qualifying transactions as hedges for accounting purposes. &nbsp;This section builds on Accounting Guideline AcG-13, &#147;Hedging Relationships,&#148; and Section 1650, &#147;Foreign Currency Translation&#148;. &nbsp;The Company does not use hedge accounting and has no hedging relationships.</P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px" align=justify>Section 1535- Capital Disclosures &#150; This section establishes standards for disclosing information about an entity&#146;s capital and how it is managed. &nbsp;It requires the disclosure of the entity&#146;s objectives, policies and processes for managing capital as well as summary quantitative data on the elements included in the management of capital. </P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px" align=justify>Section 3031 &#150; Inventories &#150; This section establishes standards for measuring the inventories. &nbsp;The new standards require that the inventories shall be measured at the lower of cost and the net realizable value. &nbsp;This section provides guidelines on the determination of cost and its subsequent recognition as an expense, including any write-down to net realizable value and reversal of a previous write-down when the value of inventories is evidently increased due to the change in economic circumstances. &nbsp;The use of last-in, first-out method (LIFO) in measuring inventories is not recommended. This section applies to interim and annual financial statements for fiscal years beginning on or after January 1, 2008. &nbsp;The Company is evaluating the effect of adopting this new standard.</P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px" align=justify>Section 3064 &#150;Goodwill and Intangible Assets&#150; The replacement of Section 3062 establishes standards for the recognition, measurement, presentation and disclosure of goodwill and intangible assets. &nbsp;The Company is evaluating the impact of this new standard.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><BR>
<BR></P>
</DIV><DIV style="width:600px"><P style="line-height:10pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-13.333px; font-size:8pt">ALDA 2008-03-30 Q1 MD&amp;A</P>

<P style="margin:0px" align=center>FOR THE THREE MONTH PERIOD ENDED SEPTEMBER 30, 2008</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-bottom:4px; border-bottom:1px solid #000000" align=center><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:11.267px"><B>1.14b &nbsp;&nbsp;FUTURE CHANGES IN ACCOUNTING POLICIES </B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px" align=justify>As announced by the Canadian Accounting Standards Board (&#147;AcSB&#148;), the financial reporting requirements for Canadian companies will be changed to the use of International Financial Reporting Standards (&#147;IFRS&#148;), replacing Canada&#146;s own GAAP. &nbsp;The changeover date for publicly-listed companies is 2011. &nbsp;The Company has begun reviewing the IFRS for 2011. &nbsp;At this time, the Company has not yet determined the financial reporting impact due to the change of new reporting standards.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px"><B>1.15 &nbsp;&nbsp;FINANCIAL INSTRUMENTS </B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:12.6pt; margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px" align=justify>The Company's financial instruments consist of cash and equivalents, accounts receivable, subscriptions receivable, accounts payable and accrued liabilities. The fair value of these instruments approximates their carrying values except where otherwise noted. It is management's opinion that the Company is not exposed to significant interest, currency, or credit risk arising from these financial instruments except where otherwise noted.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:384px"><B>1.16</B></P>

<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px" align=justify>Additional information relating to the Company can be found on the Canadian Securities Administrators&#146; System for Electronic Document Analysis and Retrieval (SEDAR) database at www.sedar.com.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px" align=justify>Additional relevant disclosure, such as expensed research and development costs, general and administration expenses, material costs, whether capitalized, deferred or expensed are disclosed in the accompanying financial statements for the three month period ended September 30, 2008 as allowed in NI 51-102, Section 5.3 (3).</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>

<P style="margin:0px; padding-bottom:4px; border-bottom:1px solid #000000" align=center><BR></P>

<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px"><B>1.16</B></P>
<P style="line-height:22pt; margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px; text-indent:32.867px"><B>OTHER MD&amp;A REQUIRMENTS (continued)</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:38px; padding-right:-7.6px; text-indent:-32px" align=justify><B>(c)</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:38px; padding-right:-7.6px" align=justify><B>Disclosure Controls and Procedures </B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px" align=justify>The management of ALDA is responsible for establishing and maintaining disclosure controls and procedures for the Company and has designed such disclosure controls and procedures, or caused them to be designed under ALDA management&#146;s supervision, to provide reasonable assurance that material information relating to the Company, including its consolidated subsidiaries, is made known to ALDA management by others within those entities particularly during the period covered by this MD&amp;A.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px" align=justify>ALDA management has evaluated the effectiveness of the Company&#146;s disclosure controls and procedures for the period covered by this MD&amp;A and based on that evaluation, the management has concluded that the disclosure controls and procedures are effective.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-right:-7.6px" align=justify><B>&nbsp;(d) &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Internal Control Over Financial Reporting</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px" align=justify>The Company&#146;s management is responsible for establishing and maintaining adequate internal control over financial reporting. &nbsp;Management has considered the effectiveness of design of the Company&#146;s internal controls and procedures over financial reporting and has noted weaknesses in internal controls over financial reporting such as a lack of segregation of duties because of limited staff members.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px" align=justify>Management intends to initiate steps to remedy the noted shortcomings over the next fiscal year by carrying out a management assessment of the weaknesses with a view to improving areas where weaknesses exist and implementing procedures aimed at minimizing the risk of material error in its financial reporting.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px"><B>1.17 &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;SUBSEQUENT EVENTS &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:4.933px; padding-right:-7.6px" align=justify>Subsequent to the three month period ended September 30, 2008, the Company granted incentive stock options to certain directors, senior officers, employees and consultants to purchase an aggregate of 550,000 common shares at an exercise price of $0.20 and a term of five years, expiring on October 31, 2008.</P>

<P style="line-height:14pt; margin-top:16px; margin-bottom:-18.667px; padding-left:48px; text-indent:-48px; font-size:12pt" align=justify><B><I>2.</I></B></P>

<P style="line-height:14pt; margin-top:16px; margin-bottom:-18.667px; padding-left:48px; text-indent:-48px; font-size:12pt" align=justify><B><I>3.</I></B></P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin:0px; padding-left:48px; font-size:12pt" align=justify><B><I>Fair presentation:</I></B><I> &nbsp;</I>Based on my knowledge, having exercised reasonable diligence, the interim financial statements together with the other financial information included in the interim filings fairly present in all material respects the financial condition, results of operations and cash flows of the issuer, as of the date of and for the periods presented in the interim filings.</P>

<TR><TD style="border:1px solid #000000" valign=top width=918.067><P style="margin-top:13.333px; margin-bottom:0px" align=center><B><U>NOTE TO READER</U></B></P>
<P style="margin-top:13.333px; margin-bottom:0px" align=justify>In contrast to the certificate required for non-venture issuers under Multilateral Instrument 52-109 <I>Certification of Disclosure in Issuers&#146; Annual and Interim Filings </I>(MI 52-109), this Venture Issuer Basic Certificate does not include representations relating to the establishment and maintenance of disclosure controls and procedures (DC&amp;P) and internal control over financial reporting (ICFR), as defined in MI 52-109. In particular, the certifying officers filing this certificate are not making any representations relating to the establishment and maintenance of:</P>
<P style="margin-top:13.333px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:72px; text-indent:-48px" align=justify>i)</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:72px" align=justify>controls and other procedures designed to provide reasonable assurance that information required to be disclosed by the Issuer in its annual filings, interim filings or other reports filed or submitted under securities legislation is recorded, processed, summarized and reported within the time periods specified in securities legislation; and</P>
<P style="margin-top:13.333px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:72px; text-indent:-48px" align=justify>ii)</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:72px" align=justify>a process to provide reasonable assurance regarding the reliability of financial reporting and the preparation of financial statements for external purposes in accordance with the Issuer&#146;s GAAP.</P>
<P style="margin-top:13.333px; margin-bottom:0px" align=justify>The Issuer&#146;s certifying officers are responsible for ensuring that processes are in place to provide them with sufficient knowledge to support the representations they are making in this certificate.</P>
<P style="margin-top:13.333px; margin-bottom:0px" align=justify>Investors should be aware that inherent limitations on the ability of certifying officers of a venture issuer to design and implement on a cost effective basis DC&amp;P and ICFR as defined in MI 52-109 may result in additional risks to the quality, reliability, transparency and timeliness of interim and annual filings and other reports provided under securities legislation. </P>
</TD></TR>

<P style="line-height:14pt; margin-top:16px; margin-bottom:0px; font-family:Times New Roman Bold; font-size:12pt" align=center><B>CERTIFICATION OF INTERIM FILINGS</B></P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin-top:16px; margin-bottom:0px; font-size:12pt" align=center><B>Venture Issuer Basic Certificate</B></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin-top:16px; margin-bottom:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>I, Peter Chen<I>,</I><B><I> </I></B>the Chief Financial Officer of ALDA Pharmaceuticals Corp., certify the following:</P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin-top:16px; margin-bottom:-18.667px; padding-left:48px; text-indent:-48px; font-size:12pt" align=justify><B><I>1.</I></B></P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin:0px; padding-left:48px; font-size:12pt" align=justify><B><I>Review:</I></B><I> &nbsp;</I>I have reviewed the interim financial statements and interim MD&amp;A (together the interim filings) of <B><I>ALDA Pharmaceuticals Corp. </I></B>(the &#147;Issuer&#148;) for the interim period ended <B><I>September 30, 2008</I></B>.</P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin-top:16px; margin-bottom:-18.667px; padding-left:48px; text-indent:-48px; font-size:12pt" align=justify><B><I>2.</I></B></P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin:0px; padding-left:48px; font-size:12pt" align=justify><B><I>No misrepresentations:</I></B> &nbsp;Based on my knowledge, having exercised reasonable diligence, the interim filings do not contain any untrue statement of a material fact or omit to state a material fact required to be stated or that is necessary to make a statement not misleading in light of the circumstances under which it was made, for the period covered by the interim filings.</P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin-top:16px; margin-bottom:-18.667px; padding-left:48px; text-indent:-48px; font-size:12pt" align=justify><B><I>3.</I></B></P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin:0px; padding-left:48px; font-size:12pt" align=justify><B><I>Fair presentation:</I></B><I> &nbsp;</I>Based on my knowledge, having exercised reasonable diligence, the interim financial statements together with the other financial information included in the interim filings fairly present in all material respects the financial condition, results of operations and cash flows of the issuer, as of the date of and for the periods presented in the interim filings.</P>

<P style="margin-top:13.333px; margin-bottom:0px" align=justify>In contrast to the certificate required for non-venture issuers under Multilateral Instrument 52-109 <I>Certification of Disclosure in Issuers&#146; Annual and Interim Filings </I>(MI 52-109), this Venture Issuer Basic Certificate does not include representations relating to the establishment and maintenance of disclosure controls and procedures (DC&amp;P) and internal control over financial reporting (ICFR), as defined in MI 52-109. In particular, the certifying officers filing this certificate are not making any representations relating to the establishment and maintenance of:</P>
<P style="margin-top:13.333px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:72px; text-indent:-48px" align=justify>iii)</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:72px" align=justify>controls and other procedures designed to provide reasonable assurance that information required to be disclosed by the Issuer in its annual filings, interim filings or other reports filed or submitted under securities legislation is recorded, processed, summarized and reported within the time periods specified in securities legislation; and</P>
<P style="margin-top:13.333px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:72px; text-indent:-48px" align=justify>iv)</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:72px" align=justify>a process to provide reasonable assurance regarding the reliability of financial reporting and the preparation of financial statements for external purposes in accordance with the Issuer&#146;s GAAP.</P>
<P style="margin-top:13.333px; margin-bottom:0px" align=justify>The Issuer&#146;s certifying officers are responsible for ensuring that processes are in place to provide them with sufficient knowledge to support the representations they are making in this certificate.</P>
<P style="margin-top:13.333px; margin-bottom:0px" align=justify>Investors should be aware that inherent limitations on the ability of certifying officers of a venture issuer to design and implement on a cost effective basis DC&amp;P and ICFR as defined in MI 52-109 may result in additional risks to the quality, reliability, transparency and timeliness of interim and annual filings and other reports provided under securities legislation. </P>
